<Author>PRTravelerAllTheTime
<Content>Traveler be warned! First let me say that I travel to Puerto Rico monthly for business and I have stayed at the Normandie seven or eight times. I have encountered all of the following problems there: FILTHY rooms that stink and have trash, etc. left from previous guests; toilets won't flush; thermostats don't work; so much moisture in the room that mold and mildew are growing on every surface; broken refrigerators and microwaves; I started carrying Lysol with me on each trip in an effort to avoid illness; mildewed shower curtains; extremely noisy - parties in the atrium that are WAY too loud, even during the week; totally unresponsive front desk and manager who just looks at you when you ask questions/make complaints; I was overbilled more than once; even after my company paid a direct billed stay, I found a credit card charge on my personal charge TWO MONTHS after a stay at this hotel - it took me almost two more months to get anyone to respond (and then someone from my company locally had to go in to the hotel and protest on my behalf). After many complaints, my colleagues and I now stay at the Condado Plaza - it's not perfect, but it's WAY better than this place. CONSIDER YOURSELF WARNED - and watch out for the falling plaster from the side of the building - that really dinged up my rental car on one of my last stays!

<Author>FunshineSunshine
<Content>Made the Best of It We just returned from an 8 day vacation in Puerto Rico at the Normandie Hotel. The hotel is not what I thought it would be. My room was on the 4th floor and did not have a balcony. It was disappointing to see an unsightly, rusty roofed building behind the hotel between my room and the beach, partially blocking my oceanview. My hotel room windows consisted of several small window panes. All but two were sealed shut and the two that would open, would not stay open unless you held or propped them up with something. There was no beach area to speak of behind the hotel. It was more like a rocky shoreline and was mainly blocked because of the other building behind the hotel. There was an outdoor swimming pool but nothing fancy, no hot tub, towels, etc., and it was surrounded by a painted white concrete wall. The pool was located on the far left, rear side of the hotel. That was the only available space for it. Once we entered the hotel all we saw were walls. There were no windows on the first floor to view anything outside of the hotel. Hotel entertainment was less than desirable and the advertised continental breakfast cost $12.00 per person. A regular cup of coffee cost over $4.00. The dining area was not an actual restaurant, but rather an open area in the middle of the first floor. On the good side, our room wasn't bad. Our bed and pillows were very comfortable, and the hotel was very clean. The maid service was outstanding, plenty of fresh, plush towels everyday. Most, if not all, hotel workers are uniformed or wear suits. Hotel workers were very polite; not all workers were friendly but they were polite. If you're looking for a reasonably priced, clean, classy, secluded, escape-from-the-world type hotel, the Normandie is for you. Our mistake was booking a hotel, and expecting resort amenities. Because of that, we didn't spend much time at the Normandie. Instead, we ventured over to the local resorts and enjoyed thier amenities, shops, restaurants, etc. I would certainly recommend the Normandie to people looking for a hotel, not a resort.  
<Date>Oct 25, 2008

<Author>trippinCrownPoint_In
<Content>BOO-Tique Hotel My stepdaughter  i booked a trip to San Juan for 7/24 to 7/27 thru Travelocity. Our plane was due in @ 5:30am on the 24th, not wanting to wait 9 or so hours for our room to be ready i preemptively PURCHASED ( not reserved- purchased) a room thru hotel.com for the 23rd which in my mind meant that i would have a hotel room from 3pm(check-in) on 7/23 til 12pm(checkout) on 7/24 at which time my package would be closer to kicking in so surely they would just leave us in the room we were in. Silly me! Our planes was delayed twice so we didn't arrive til 8am. We got to the hotel Noramandie only to be told that our room had been given away because we were considered a no-show. Needless to say i hit the roof questioning how they could give away a room that was PAID for. I went round  round with the front desk staff  manager til my weary from travelin mind couldn't take it anymore, i ended up having to call hotels.com who straightened things out. Oh but it gets worse.. After ending their call with hotels.com I was informed by the staff that unfortunately they didn't have our requested double bed room. Again showing them my receipt i questioned why they didn't have what i payed for. I was told that a request is just that a request, it's not guaranteed. In lieu of the double beds that we requested we where offered a cot, still weary from the long travel  with no fight left in me i said whatever just give me the key to my room I'm tired. We get to our room and open the door  the most overwhelming smell of mildew smacks us in the face. For the most part the hotel  rooms look just like the pictures on the net, however you cant see how filthy the carpet is through out the property. I wouldn't have dared to walk on the floor in our room bare footed. You cant see the thick layering of dust that covered the air conditioning vent in our room from the pics on the net either. I woke up the next morning with severe sinus congestion and the day after that I woke up with a rash on my face! Oh did i mention that they brought us the crappiest cot that i've ever seen in my life. Not that I'm a connoisseur of cots but this thing was so antiquated that it looked like something from the 50's, so we ended up sharing the king bed. We really didn't hang around the hotel that much because there was nothing to do there, at one point we sat in the lounge area for an hour  not one soul passed by. For entertainment we spent some time next door at the Hilton as their lounge area was filled with people dancing and having a good time. With the exception of a class reunion that reserved the only club in the hotel on the 26th(it was closed to the other hotel guests) the place was virtually void of people which is another reason why i just couldn't understand why we couldn't have the room the we reserved and purchased. I am of the opinion that they don't have rooms with double beds because that hotel was by no means booked up. The Normandie is an old hotel that somebody slapped a few coats of paint on  added some contemporary furniture to. Its by no means a 3 1/2 to 4 star hotel and its highly over priced. The best part of the Normandie is the lounge area which is nicely decorated (even though the carpet is FILTHY) the bartender there was really nice, also the 2 concierges were helpful. The worst things about the Normandie are the front desk staff , the manger, the filthy floors, and the mildewed smelling room. I would recommend this hotel to someone that i didn't like. CAUTION: Personal items were stolen from my checked suitcase at the San Juan Airport!! My travels didn't end there as i left for Jamaica on the 29th of July.Check out my review of the new Grand Palladium!

<Author>maestraWisconsin
<Content>Wonderful! I stayed with a friend for 8 nights. I was a bit scared after reading many of the other reviews but I was pleasantly surprised. It was nothing like the horrible things I read about. The staff was always friendly and incredibly bilingual (we do speak Spanish but they used mostly English with us). The room was clean and freshened daily. The pool area is not a resort pool area but it has lounge chairs and tables. It was a clean and nice pool, although not large. The beach is not impressive but the hotel is close to the public beaches (basically right next door). If you really want a beach experience, I'd suggest taking the bus to Isla Verde where there is a sandy bottom and tons of nice public beaches. The food at the hotel was very good but we found a lot of really nice places within walking distance on the Condado beach strip. The location of the hotel was perfect for us. We could catch the bus or walk into Old San Juan (I'd recommend not walking the first day like we did...). We walked to dinner every night and back and it was only about a mile or so each way, depending on where we ate. Overall, I am very happy with this hotel and would stay there again without hesitation.

<Author>momokekeke
<Content>ok overall This hotel turned out to be better than I had expected. The staff was friendly and the room was clean and spacious. <Author>2bythec
<Content>This old ship needs some love This lovely old hotel has great potential - but fails to deliver. Indeed, as noted in other reviews, the staff are terribly rude and I felt the whole time they did not want us there. Also, as noted by others, there was no washcloths and even after repeated requests for fresh towels and facecloths, we gave up on waiting. They also pulled the no more than 3 persons in the room line with us upon check in. Coffee, if you are interested, will cost you almost 5$ for a single cup (go across the street to the Subway instead for a $3 breaky including coffee). The hotel was very smelly (musty) and very dirty (the carpets are flithy). Yet, the rooms are large though and the decor is lovely. This place screams potential but is in sad shape overall. As other reviews have stated, it is a costly $10 taxi ride to town. Or, you can hike it for under 25 minutes if you cut through the park or grab a bus for 0.50 cents almost across from the hotel. In Old San Juan, you can take the trolley, the bus, or the ferry to explore (all better options than the cab).The beach behind the hotel is flithy. Garbage everywhere and even dirty diapers strewn beach-side.On the upside...The Concierage was a little friendlier than anyone else encountered there and can be somewhat helpful. Also, the pool was very nice. If you want to enjoy the area's view, slip out on the balconey through the excercise room.Overall, it was not so bad... if you can get past the staff, the smell, and the dirty carpets... focus instead on the decor, and the history of the old place (which was modeled after a ship; one where the original owner had met his wife - they say the hotel was a love letter to her).

<Author>SouthSide10
<Content>Horrendous Service My wife and I stayed at the Normandie along with two other couples, all in for a mutual friend's wedding. The hotel is very easy on the eyes, but in a somewhat inconvenient location because you need a cab to get to either a nice beach or to Old San Juan. The hotel has a beach, but it is very small. You're much better off getting to a beach east of the Normadie during the day. That said, we had many problems with the service. In fact, this was the worst service we have ever experienced in a hotel. We were told by soon-to-be-wed friend that she had left a San Juan welcome kit at the Front Desk. We didn't get the welcome kit until we checked out and that was only after asking 4 different employees. Also, the breakfast service in one of the hotel's restaurants was equally atrocius. Not a single wait staff led us to a table or offered us a drink. At the end, when we went to pay for the buffet (which was not complimentary), we could not even get the attention of the wait staff. We left without paying for the below-average food. Finally, when we complained at the check-out about our bad experience, the manager on duty offered us a free meal at the same restaurant where the wait staff ignored us. We declined and vowed to write this review. If we had to do it again, we would have booked a hotel in Old San Juan. There are restaurants, museums, and bars, which cannot be said for the area around the Normadie. If you want to visit a beach around San Juan, it's just as easy to take a cab from Old San Juan as the Normadie. San Juan was fantastic, as was the rest of Puerto Rico we saw (Culebra, Fajardo, the food, the people, the culture). The Normandie was an oustandingly poor exception. If we have the opportunity to go back to San Juan again, it would take a lot for us to darken their door again.

<Content>A Good Value for the Price I booked the Normandie after seeing that it was recommended in Frommer's Guide for one night prior to departing on a cruise out of San Juan. <Author>LOTRfan
<Content>Decent enough hotel I have mixed feelings about my stay at this hotel. The staff were excellent and very helpful. When I had problems with their WiFi (it didn't work) or when I accidentally broke one of the shade cords in my room, they were very prompt (in 5 minutes) in fixing the problem. <Author>JRSchlumpf
<Content>Disappointing Hotel - Stay Next Door at the Caribe Hilton This was our second visit to the Normandie (first visit in February, 2006) and it will be our last. It is a grand old hotel in need of some loving care. On our first visit, two years ago, we really enjoyed the art deco styling and the beach and diving adjacent to the property all for a price that was very reasonable (we paid about $160 this time). This time however, was very different. There was a lot of noisy construction underway inside the hotel and there had been some water damage in our room so it smelled very musty. Everything seemed run down and just not of the quality we remembered. On our last day we walked next door to the Caribe Hilton and it was everything you want in a hotel, all for only about $30 more per night. Trust me, that would be money well spent.

<Author>TheHall
<Content>Not a bad hotel We stayed one night at the Normandie and had an alright experience. We were staying in San Juan one night prior to our cruise. The staff was very friendly upon arrival and very curtious. Our room was on the third floor, towards the back. The room was averaged size with a small room off to the side with a desk. The furniture did look like it came from an Ikea catalog, but the room was clean. The rug did look old but looked clean. It is and old building and the plumbing is probalby old as well, we could hear every time some one next to/or above us flushed but not a big deal. The noise did radiate from the night club around 130am, again nothing terrible. Over all it was a clean place, friendly staff, some noise but not terrible. I would not stay here for an entire vacation (there is nothing really around this area), but for one night it was ok. I would also not pay $300/night, we booked through price line for $140, that seemed reasonable for this place, although, this is not a 3 star hotel. We can not attest to the food, we ate at subway and had breakfast at Starbucks in the Hilton next door.

<Author>maharaniDC
<Content>Believe the Awful Reviews on This Site This hotel is absolutely awful. We stayed in a business class room and payed $200/night. It was dingy, very little light, next to the lounge that is noisy at night, the shower leaked all over the floor every time we used it, the carpet and the couches were dirty and had stains, and the entire room smelled and felt of mildew. It was so dirty that I didn't want to walk around without shoes on. The front desk was helpful in a couple of instances, but also not helpful when we had a few other questions - so with service, the Normandie is hit or miss. The continental breakfast is OK - not bad, not great. I really wished I did not stay at this hotel. Its completely not worth your money. There is no reason to stay here since there are plenty of other places around that are just as close to the places you want to see in Old San Juan. Do not give this hotel your money - the reviews on this site do not exaggerate. The only possibly redeeming quality of the place was that after two straight nights of having loud neighbors, we asked to be moved and were put in a top floor suite with a view of the ocean. This room was clean and had a good shower. I suppose if you are willing to pay alot more than $200, you might be lucky enough to get a clean room with a shower that does not leak.

<Author>Cutternsanchez
<Content>Love/hate relationship I'm stunned after staying recently at the Normandie and now, after our trip, reading the other Tripadvisor reviews and comments. Did we stay at the same hotel?!? Was there a massive makeover right before we got there?!?I believe it's all about expectations. If you're the stereo-typical American traveler expecting a modern hotel where everyone speaks fluent English and jumps when you raise your voice....or if you're expecting a mega-hotel with a casino, multiple dining options, and a long list of amenities....or if you're one of those cruise ship types just passing through before or after a boat.....this is probably NOT the hotel for you. I chose this hotel for a group of my friends and I after researching a list of about 20 hotels in the San Juan (Old Town to Isle Verde) region. If I wanted a mega, Vegas-like hotel, I would have booked the Marriott. If I'd wanted more beach, I would have booked in the Condado or Isle Verde area. [Aside: take the comments about the airport noise VERY SERIOUSLY in the Isle Verde region.]My friends and I like unique experiences, and I think we got it at the Normandie. I would call this a boutique hotel if I had to slap a label on it. Like most of the other reviewers, I'll give props to the cool retro lobby/atrium. The hotel's food was excellent all around. We loved Sylvia in the lobby restaurant and Paloma in the restaurant Red. [Tell Paloma Sorry we didn't come back on Wednesday. We didn't win the Lottery.] You should definitely do Red with friends and try a bunch of the menu items (e.g. tuna tartare, lamb tapas, etc.). One of the top meals I had in San J. Unlike some of the other reviewers, my room (#307) was wonderful. It was clean, very comfortable, and maybe because it was slightly off-atrium, it was quiet. I thought it had a great view of the little bay and ocean also. [Another Aside to all those Experienced travelers: ALWAYS negotiate your taxi fare before you get in and be ready to walk away. They almost never pass up a fair fare. You got ripped off paying $20 to Old Town and Condado. And we only paid $18 for two of us to get to the far side of Isle Verde. ALWAYS ask the doorman/conceirge/bellman what's a reasonable rate to your destination. THANKS Angel!!!]Let's see.....ahh, the negatives: 1.Yes, the lobby/atrium was a little cold. 2. A couple of my friends said that the walls were a little thin since some party-ers next to them kept them up until 3 a.m.....but then they said that it may have been the noise coming through the door ajoining the two rooms.3. It could use some renovations, but then what 60 year old building couldn't. Be careful of the windows in room 307. They're weird, you'll see.The Normandie was unique.....and uniquely Puerto Rican!!! Keep an open mind if you book there. And try not to act like a stereotypical American. I was embarrassed by the attitudes of some other compatriot guests I saw in the lobby.1

<Author>RetiredProsecutor
<Content>A Last Resort We arrived here after a two week cruise through the Panama Canal and the two day stay was pretty much a disaster. The art-deco building has possibilities, but a close look reveals deferred maintenance issues -- dirty carpets, gouged plaster, peeling paint, and broken plumbing fixtures in the rooms. Because we arrived here during the San Sebastian festival, and every decent hotel was jam packed, we took a chance and made reservations here. This is clearly the very worst $300@night hotel we had ever stayed in. It's like a haunted house, you almost never see other people and definitely never see any hotel staff, who simply don't seem to be around, and if they are, aren't particularly service-oriented. Meanwhile the wind blows across the glass roof creating howls and metallic creaking noises. When you or a neighboring room flushes the toilet, air ducts in the ceiling start rattling. To be completely fair, with the exception of the carpets, the place seems more or less clean.The service is so bad here that you feel like you are the dupe on Candid Camera. The desk clerk declined to answer my questions, instead referring me to the concierge in training - a bellhop who didn't speak understandable English. (Yes, this is Puerto Rico but after all, he IS in the hospitality industry and this IS the USA. I found more English spoken in Western Europe than in San Juan.) This concierge didn't even know if their hotel restaurant served breakfast! I asked him about nearby church services and attractions and got a blank look.A few examples will serve: (1) we asked for sugar for our in-room coffee - 30 minutes later it hadn't arrived - when I went down to the desk they insisted they would send it up again - would not hand me some - we never did get the sugar; (2) departure morning I called for a bellhop to help me and my ailing wife bring down our luggage -- he never showed up and we schlepped them ourselves; (3) the night before the departure, I asked for a wakeup call in room 725 at 6 am -- in broken English the receptionist said, OK, wake you up at 7 in room 724. I corrected him and he brusquely replied that it was taken care of. We never did get that call -- I feel sorry for whatever room got that call; (4) I asked them to have a taxi downstairs for us - they didn't. It's like this place doesn't care about repeat business.Furthermore, this hotel is centrally located, i.e. its not close to anything at all. You want to go to a pharmacy, see the city's attractions, go to a grocery store, or eat at a non-hotel restaurant -- only choice is to take a taxi either eastbound to Condado or westbound to Old San Juan. But they do have a hotel store that will sell you a soft drink for $5 a can. Maybe I caught them at a bad time --- but the few guests I interacted with during my stay were saying the same things.

<Author>seetheworld25
<Content>Awful Hotel, Would Never Recommend I have never had such a negative experience at a hotel as I did when we stayed two nights at the Normandie. I would NEVER recommend this hotel to anyone, and strongly caution anyone from staying there.Our first impressions of the hotel were good, the lobby was nice and very art-deco. However, we were disgusted when we opened the door to our room. There were little tiny bugs crawling all over surfaces in the room, rust on anything metal in the room, and paint was chipped off the walls. Our shower looked like it hadn't been cleaned, as there was some kind of liquid (looked like body wash) drizzled down the side of the bath tub. The toilet only flushed when you held down the handle for ten seconds and even then a lot of times you had to flush twice. In the mornings there was no hot water and we took cold showers two mornings in a row. When we opened our blinds to look out the window, we discovered dirty kleenex behind the blinds. It was absolutely disgusting. For the money we paid, we expected a four star hotel as they claim they are. I would have classified it a 2 star.The gross room wasn't the least of our problems at the Normandie, though. We had booked our stay for two nights over the phone and were given a confirmation number. We had re-confirmed that reservation just 3 days before arriving, and everything was set. However, on the second night at about 5:00, we received a call from the front desk telling us we needed to check out immediately or face a $50 late check out fee. I argued and said we had a reservation for 2 nights, but since I had no proof other than the confirmation number, they continued to insist I check out, as they had no availability for that night. I asked to speak to the manager several times, but he refused to speak with me. One time he came out of his office, looked at me, said something to the front desk clerk in Spanish, and then walked back into the office. I thought that was the most ridiculous thing I've ever seen, I couldn't believe a manager refused to talk to a guest. Remarkably they found a room, but I had to pay twice what our regular rate was for it. I was absolutely livid, but we didn't have a choice at that point and had to pay the rate in order to have a place to stay that night. Being an experienced traveler, I have a feeling that they didn't want to honor our discounted rate for that night and decided to con us into paying more. Our travel agent told us that happens a lot in Mexico and the Caribbean, so I would bet that's what happened. So moral to the story: if you book over the phone, always get something additional in print!Our nightmare continued that second night when the hotel hosted a pre-New Years Eve party for the locals (I would bet only about 10% of the hotels guests actually went to the party). We were given no notification about this when we made the reservation or at check-in other than that the restaurant would be closed for setting it up. What was ridiculous was that they hosted it in the atrium, and the hotel is set up so that all floors of the hotel look down into the atrium, so the noise traveled up. There were hundreds of people there which was loud enough, but then the band started playing at 10:00 and went until 1:15 am. They had to have had the speakers on the loudest possible volume. We were on the third floor and our furniture was vibrating. It was perhaps the most inconsiderate thing I have ever seen a hotel do. The purpose of a hotel is to have a place to sleep, and how could anyone sleep when there is a band blaring. I was particularly upset because we had to get up early the next morning. When I called to complain, the front desk clerk was rude and just told me the music will be off by 1:00, which should give you plenty of rest. It wasn't off by 1, though... the band kept playing encores and then people hung around in the atrium after that and the noise still came up into our room.When we checked out the next day I complained again about the noise but wasn't given any apology or compensation. Overall the rooms were gross, the customer service was awful, and it seemed to be a very corrupt hotel. It is extremely over priced, yet I don't think even if it was cheaper I would ever recommend the Normandie. This hotel was truly a nightmare experience.

<Content>Beautiful space but poorly managed Loved the lobby and had no problems with the room once we got in the room....We requested a non-smoking room with two beds on an upper floor (paying extra for a suite) and we were given a smoke-saturated room on the second floor with one king bed. After a friendly but firm conversation with the manager, we were moved up to a non-smoking room with two beds on the 7th floor (after being told that there were no other rooms available). This hotel could and should be a 4-star but it needs to improve its service. We couldn't even get a cup of coffee in the morning because the restaurant was understaffed (the buffet bar was cluttered with dirty plates and the coffee urns were empty by 10am???). So we took our dollars to the Hilton Caribe next door for breakfast.On the second night, the hotel teamed up with a local radio station for a pre-New Year's Eve event--which meant loud pounding music in the 7-story atrium pouring all the way up into the rooms. It was great to see lots of people having fun in the lobby but the noise spilled into the rooms (and the live music did not stop until 1am). The hotel management did not consider the comfort of the paying guests when they organized this event. After this experience, I don't trust they are able to provide a high level of service you would come to expect from a 300plus/per night room.

<Author>TerrySisk
<Content>Landmark Art Deco Hotel This circa 1942 hotel is not for everyone. Although its swimming pool sits between the hotel and the ocean, it's possible to stay at the Normandie for a week and not even realize it has a swimming pool, not to mention a beachfront location. This hotel looks inward, not out to sea. The hotel's view is the atrium lobby itself, seven stories high and capped by an enormous skylight. Like a Hyatt Regency, all rooms are accessed from hallways that overhang the perimeter of the atrium. In this case the guard rails are designed to recall the exterior deck rails on an ocean liner, specifically the S.S. Normandie (the Puerto Rican builder of this hotel met his French bride aboard this ship). The hotel has achieved national historic landmark status, so the authentic architectural details are here to stay, although the polychromed colors are gone, now favoring pastel blue grays that lighten the effect considerably.Other reviewers complain about the lack of restaurants in the area, yet the Caribe Hilton next door boasts no fewer than seven restaurants in all price ranges, poolside as well as indoors. The adjacent Escambron public beach has a sea-front restaurant that specializes in Puerto Rican cuisine. The Normandie is a five minute taxi ride to Old San Juan's music venues, bars, shops and restaurants (tourists staying in Isla Verde's resorts pay double the cab fare and waste 25 minutes each way to/from Old San Juan).All that said, the Normandie is not a resort, nor is it a hotel for families with children, who would get bored quickly. It is an incredible bargain (booking directly through the hotel's web site yielded a rate of $135 per night per room during Thanksgiving week -- other hotel booking sites were quoting $179 or more) for a first class hotel. The hallways are a virtual gallery of original art. There is a hip club on the second floor that attracts classy locals. A la carte breakfasts are delicious (forget the lackluster buffet) and imaginative. The rooms are large and supremely comfortable. The small sitting rooms with desks or day beds were obviously once outdoor lanais, since their floors slope downward (drainage would have required that). Furnishings are high end -- even the ergonomic Herman Miller desk chair retails for $450. The bathrooms are spacious, functional and clean but lack the glamour of the room's interior furnishings.As for the complaints about location, if you want to stay put at an all-inclusive resort, go to Jamaica or the Dominican Republic. It would be a crime to go to San Juan and not visit Condado, Isla Verde and Old San Juan (located miles apart) -- so budget some taxi money or learn to use the absurdly cheap public bus system. I have stayed at the El San Juan Hotel, Intercontinental Resort, El Convento, Water Club -- as well as the charming At Wind Chimes Inn. For my money, the Normandie is the best bargain of them all. I'm staying here again on my next visit to San Juan.Note to those who booked by Priceline and mentioned a $10 per night surcharge for utilities -- that's an absurd practice that should be reported to Priceline. No such fee was added to my bill -- only taxes amounting to approx. 10%. Also, because this hotel does not have a casino, the extra 10% charge assessed by casino hotels does not apply.Terry Sisk

<Author>mlbadvisor
<Content>Could've been better... What you need to know about PR:--definitely visit PR. beautiful island, great people, great food, rainforest is beautiful and visitor-friendly, caves are gorgeous. be prepared to spend money on (a) cabs and/or (b) a rental car.On to the Normandie:--this is not a 3.5/4 star hotel. --our stay was enjoyable, but this hotel (unlike the Caribe Hilton next door) is not a vacation/getaway in and of itself. the pool is tiny, which didn't bother me as much as the fact that the surrounding sunbathing area is tiny as well. besides that, the entire pool area is basically in disrepair.--the hotel is not close to anything. the Caribe Hilton has a few restaurants, which is where we went to eat. Normandie restaurant is OK, but overpriced for the amount of food you get. At least at the Hilton, you are shelling out $$ but receiving a good portion of food in return. the service at both the Normandie and Caribe Hilton leaves something to be desired.--it will cost you $20/RT to old san juan, and about $20/RT to condado. a RT to isla verde will be between $30-$40. since there's a paucity of food options around the hotel, you may be cabbing it a whole lot.--the hotel abuts a tiny strip of public beach full of garbage, crabs, and local fishermen/folks looking to blow some time. it's only about 20 feet long, and the tide is high enough at all times to prevent anyone from laying out there (not that you would want to, trust me).--the hotel is adjacent to a public beach called Escambron. it's about a 10-15 minute walk from the hotel. this isn't the pearl of the Caribbean or anything, but it's definitely a decent beach. it's usually populated with locals, and has some OK snorkeling (often little fishies would be swimming around our feet).--the staff at the Normandie is great. the doormen/concierges were always very helpful, especially in booking tours. the housekeeping was also above average.--the following would've ensured the hotel's 3.5/4 star rating in my eyes: a mirror in the hotel room (besides the one in the bathroom), the ability to open our windows, a decent poolside area, more food options, a better fridge, attention to detail (smudges all over the hotel, dirty furniture, etc.), a functioning bathroom sink, a balcony. we would walk over to the caribe hilton in the evening, buy a drink or dinner, and then walk around their beachfront facilities. i don't recommend trying to sneak into the pool during the daytime, they check for room keys.Overall:The Normandie is a pretty hotel; you can tell it once had a heyday. The staff is friendly, the room is a great size, and all of the furniture is super comfortable. Plus, at least at night, you can head over to the Hilton and enjoy a great dinner and an awesome beachfront and pier.However, if we could do PR again, we probably would not stay at the Normandie. We easily spent $150+ on cabs, and only visited the dingy pool area once. The hotel restaurant food was tasty, but badly overpriced for the portion size. No free continental breakfast, either. And the $14/day municipal fee plus hotel tariff definitely didn't help.The Normandie was a decent base of operation from which we explored PR, but next time we'll go with a hotel that is oceanfront, with a nice pool area, and in the proximity of restaurants/food/stores/local flavor.

<Author>billdaffy
<Content>Definately Not a 3.5 Star Hotel Yet This was our second trip to the Normandie Hotel- the prior visit was 2 years ago and I must say that there have been strides made to bring this hotel up to acceptable visitor standards. The hotel staff, as has been mentioned previously, seems first rate -- accommodating and pleasant, they appear to form a solid base upon which they can build a loyal following. Unfortunately, the housekeeping has not followed suit. As we entered our room the first night, the first thing that we saw was a giant roach on the ceiling. We called the front desk and shortly thereafter two members of the housekeeping staff arrived to brush the cockroach onto the floor and stepped on it. We were assured that this was very unusual and not to expect an more visitors during our stay. Unfortunately, the next morning my wife found an even larger cockroach in the tub. We called housekeeping again who assured us that they would have someone, later that day, spray the room. I assume that this was done since we didn't see anymore animal life when we were there. If it was only the roachs, you could conceivably give the hotel a pass. But the rest of the room was hardly acceptable. First there were what looked like pee stains on the chair, the room was unbeleivably dim --- need to get rid of the 25 watt bulbs !! --- the rest of the room generally looked like it was in dire need of renovation. On the positive front, the room and the hotel was very cool -- maybe even cold--- an the beds were very comfortable. All in all, an ok experience, but certainly not a 3.5 star hotel yet

<Author>Kelmya
<Content>Convenient Hotel is convenient to Condado and Old San Juan and just steps away from two very nice parks for strolling or jogging. Self-parking is affordable at $10 a day. Great staff. Rooms are comfortable with a separate work area with desk, chairs, Internet connection, etc. Although the work area is bright, the rest of the room is dark due to the type of lighting. I prefer a brighter room. The bathroom lacks a fan to reduce moisture buildup on the walls, mirror, and floor that is created when showering. The pool area can use a few plants, umbrellas, tables, etc. The pool was clean but the area where the clean pool towels are stored was not tidy. There is a daily 10% hotel tariff charge (in addition to taxes and municipal fee)which significantly increases the per day rate . The food is better than average. Overall, a nice place.

<Author>Betty76
<Content>There are better places to stay for the price! We stayed in the Normandie for 7 nights the last week of August ($1,400 total). I am not extremely picky with hotels as long as they're clean but this one did not fit the bill. When we arrived at the hotel we were extremely tired and my boys (ages 3 and 5 at the time) wanted to take a nap. Since it was 2pm I didn't think it would be a problem to get a room, the lobby employee could plainly see how tired we were but he gave me the run-around and in the end we had to walk around for 2 hours. My sister also stayed at the same hotel and she asked to be near me way in advance and they did not accomodate her request either. You can see the front desk really can do much better. The bedrooms are spacious but the carpeting and sofas are extremely dirty (dirtiest I've seen in any hotel, black stains everywhere!). The bathroom had some dried urine and feces stains on the toilet and then I almost passed out. Instead of asking for housekeeping I figured I could do a better job so I put on some gloves and wiped down the entire bathroom with disinfectant I purchased at the supermarket. One morning we left a little late in the morning and housekeeping had already skipped our room. We approached the lady and asked for our room to be cleaned anyway and she said it would be no problem. Well, we get in later that afternoon and notice our door not completely shut but when we get in the room was exactly as we left it! Obviously the cleaning lady went in and changed her mind but forgot to close the door! That's when I started going through all my things because I imagined the worst but everything was intact. The area isn't the best either, you cross the street and it's like you're in another world! We were warned not to walk around when the sun goes down so I am warning you too! The pool was ok, most days no one was there so we enjoyed it and the view of the ocean behind the pool was great too. One afternoon after swimming in the pool we noticed the back door was locked and we were told to go through the front entrace; we were in our swiiming trunks and my husband did not have a shirt on but what can you do, right? Well we walk in through the lobby and immediately upon entering the front desk employee tells my husband he can't be in the lobby without a shirt! <Author>tapdancer77
<Content>Shine's beginning to wear off... We booked this hotel on Hotwire, being promised a 3 1/2 star for our stay. I would not, however, categorize this as a 3 1/2 star hotel; maybe a 2 1/2 or a 3 star at best. In a nutshell:The Good: The hotel staff is efficient and friendly. When I asked to be moved to an upper level room (based on reviews I found here regarding N Lounge noise), they cheerfully upgraded us to a larger room on a higher floor, with a partial ocean view. The beds are quite comfortable and very easy to sleep in. The hotel was designed in a very cute chic but minimalist style. The Bad: The hotel clearly suffered during the last hurricane/tropical storm. Yes, I realize this is the Caribbean and such storms are a way of life (what are you going to do/how much rebuilding is practical), but the water damage and stains in the room were a bit extreme, even for me. Also the damage to the hotel itself was a little bad. There is no poolside bar, and no access to the beach, so no opportunity to be contacted. I would not stay here again, but probably at the Condado Plaza down the road. The hotel is also a bit isolated from the main tourist areas, so you have to call cabs everywhere. Not fun!

<Author>tekknikal
<Content>A OK Hotel if Inconsistent During the weekend where Hurricane Dean passed a couple hundred miles to the south I spent some time at this hotel with my gf and another couple. I had a room with a king bed. I didn't make the reservation but I would guess my room to be fairly average for what they have. Having said that, I enjoyed my stay overall and have no major complaints. The bed was comfortable and the room was adequately sized. There was also internet available. so my core requirements were met.Not all was perfect however, and these were the issues I had with the hotel, which I'll list in order of importance to me:-Location not so great compared to other hotels in condado area, where you could walk to a lot more places. -The bathroom seemed a little dirty- particularly on the walls, although I'm not sure if that was due to the design. -I know for many internet doesn't matter, but it does for me. The wireless access in my room seemed to not be consistently strong. Sometimes browsing was fairly quick, other times it was very slow as the signal dropped to a low level. For casual internet this would be fine. If you had high bandwidth needs for sustained periods of time it might be an issue though. -The shower had very warm (but not very hot) water on the first day. Curiously after that there was plenty of hot water. But that wasn't a big deal to me. The problem I found was that you could have soft hot water or piercing (due to the nozzle) warm water. I couldn't seem to get a soft spray of warm water. It's hard to describe here and comes off trivial as I write it, but it was a little frustrating and quite odd and led to showers that were never really very comfortable. (and im not very picky about showers!)-in room fridge not very cold at all...it was more like an insulator than anything else-On the first night there was a party on the entire ground level. This could be a good thing if you're a party person. It didn't bother me, but on the 3rd floor (of 7 iirc) it was still loud. (At ground level, it was club-like loud) I could see this being a problem for some.. the music went till early hours in the morning (I went to sleep by 1ish i think, and the music was still playing) I should note that our friends on the 4th floor didnt really hear the music but I don't see how that's possible.-Service was hit or miss - there was a party on the first night we were there. During that time we tried to get room service and no one picked up the phone. It was difficult getting through to the front desk but we did get through eventually. When we did get through, they took our order and promised to relay it to the people that do room service.. They did get the order right and in a reasonable amount of time... but when my girlfriend couldn't get through to anyone at the front desk or room service, I didn't feel good about things. They apologized for it and said it was due to the loud music... but I feel like they were dropping the ball on that as it was quickly leading to a very negative experience.overall I was fine at the hotel and didn't regret it. especially since it wasnt all that expensive, i wasnt expecting a 4/5 star experience, and the people we were with were driving around and familiar with everything. on my own i wouldnt stay here again though because of the location, internet, and just lack of overall attraction to me. but, it was reasonably comfortable and decent so overall id rate the hotel as average.

<Author>dje567
<Content>Disappointed with Normandie We selected the Normandie hotel based on reviews from other travelers and the fact that it is situated between Old San Juan and Candado/Ocean Park beaches. This was our first visit to San Juan and we learned a lot about the best locations and hotels. I was very disappointed in the Normandie. Our room had a sour smell and the carpets were quite stained. The bathroom floor needed to be cleaned as the tile grout was black with dirt (supposed to be a beige color). The drop ceilings in the room and bathroom had dust and dirt coming out of them. The pool was fine...but don't expect any drink/food service and get there early if you want a towel. Broken lounge chairs are stacked up along with various other trash items. The view of the ocean is very nice from the pool area but there is no beach (that seems safe) convenient to the hotel. The exterior of the hotel is literally crumbling in many places...this is the view you get when at the pool. The business center had leaking ceilings and empty paint cans stacked in a corner. The hotel definitely has so much potential...the art deco designs and the atrium lobby area are very cool but other details just seem to be ignored. I would recommend the Caribe Hilton located just around the corner! This hotel has its own, private beach a beautiful pool area and seemed immaculate. We ate there a couple of times as most dining seemed to be closed at Normandie. There are no local restaurants that are close to both of these hotels but the cab ride is just about 10 minutes to Old San Juan and costs about $9 each way. You can walk to the Candado beach area for a good selection of places to eat...about a 20 minute walk. Also, one reviewer said the noise was a problem at Normandie. I experienced this first-hand as there was a baby in the room next to us. She cried off and on most nights and it seemed like she was right in our room (poor sound proofing). There was a party in the 6th floor ballrooms on Friday night. We stayed on the 7th floor and the walls were shaking with the loud music until 1 a.m. We were there during 'off season' so the rest of the time the place was pretty quiet.

<Author>MrsA1990
<Content>A wonderful week! My husband and I spent a week at the Normandie (we were married there in 1990) in mid-June. We had a great business room with a big desk, internet access, a great view of the beach. Terrific kingsize bed, sitting area with a view of the beach, cable access on a good TV (not plasma, though). The staff were uniformly terrific. The only problem was housekeeping who every other day forgot something small (usually taking away dirty glasses and bringing clean ones) but they always showed up quickly with whatever was missing when we called. The food was incredible although in the Atrium cafe it was very slow coming out of the kitchen -- very fast in room service, though. But so good! High end Puerto Rican cuisine, great desserts, good solid continental breakfast. And some wonderful dishes from elsewhere (loved the Thai soup). We rented our car at the Budget desk in the lobby; always had parking. We are predisposed to love this hotel because we were married there, but the stay just didn't disappoint. A great place to work/play from.

<Author>Bill49
<Content>Fun in San Juan We stayed ath the Normandie Hotel for one night prior to our caribbean cruise on Carnival Destiny. The hotel was beautiful. The staff was very friendly, informative and helpful. We found the bar and restaurant to be a bit pricey. The room was roomy and comfortable. Some stains on the carpet were the only faults. If you stay there, talk with the local cab divers stationed outside nearby for local attractions and restaurants. They were very helpful. There is a local convenience store a block away. Beer was much cheaper there. The pool area and the lagoon was very nice. If we go back, we might picnic near the lagoon. There is a nice beach there also. We were on the fourth floor and it was very quiet. I would stay there again.

<Author>LBNashGo
<Content>We had a great time! We stayed at the Normandie only one night. It was on Sat.5/5/07, prior to our cruise  we were pleasantly surprised. From the reviews I expected something terrible  it wasn't. What we expected was loud music  a dirty hotel. Our room was quiet  the most disgusting thing I saw was soiled carpeting in the room. We came to be outdoors  not set in the hotel room. The location was good, especially being near the beautiful lagoon. It is right beside the fancy Caribe Hilton, so you can enjoy there shopping, Starbucks  gardens. We opted to not eat at the expensive steakhouse next door. Instead we spoke w/ the cab drivers  they directed us to an authentic restaurant. We hopped in a cab  were taken to the Hacienda restaurant  we walked back. The food was great  the view was magnificent. Our restaurant pictures turned out really cool. We also realized after paying $7 per beer at the Caribe, that there is a small store right across the street. At this store you can buy snacks, beer  misc. (like a Family Express) We are planning on going back next year. Just don't open your hotel window or the pigeons will try to fly in. Plus take your sunscreen  you must see the Forts in Old San Juan.

<Content>Disappointed with Normandie We stayed 1 night at the Normandie Hotel in San Juan, PR, following a caribbean cruise. We were extremely disappointed with the quality and location of the Hotel. The only food establishments nearby were Subway and Morton's Steakhouse. Any other restaurants required cab service. We were most disappointed by the additional fees charged by the Hotel. I would not recommend this hotel to other travelers.

<Author>Tuna1956
<Content>A nice stay at the Normandie Hotel We stayed 2 midweek nights at the Normandie Hotel last week, and really enjoyed the experience. The lobby and bar area as you enter is very impressive, and nicely decorated in their art deco theme. We stayed on the second floor, and our room was very large and nicely appointed. There was even a small living area just off the room, which was an added bonus! We bought cafe con leche and quesitos from Subway just across the road, and enjoyed them for breakast in our little living area. The room comes with a small fridge, and a safe too. There was entertainment in the bar area on the ground floor from 7 p.m. to 11 p.m. on Wednesday, and the singer was good. We could not hear it over our television once we were in our room. We ate at the Normandie Restaurant on our first night, and the food and service was good. Our second night, we ate at the Escambron restaurant, about 5 minutes walk away. This restaurant specializes in Puerto Rican food. The meal was very good, and about half the price of the meal we had at the Normandie Restaurant.This hotel was built in 1939, and it is on the list of Historical Landmarks. The Normandie is to be commended for preserving the feeling of that era in their decor.The only negative, in my opinion, is the lack of restaurants in the area.

<Content>Not worth the price - ok if you get significant discount We paid around $200/night (came out to around $250 with all the taxes and fees). That was way overpriced. Although the staff was nice and switched our room after we asked for an ocean view, the hotel is in serious need of a renovation. The pool area is small and somewhat dirty. There are No beach amenities - chairs, umbrellas, etc. The beach area in front of the hotel is literally the size of the pool and on weekends, it is Very crowded. We spent most of our time at the Hilton next door. There are several pools with a more lively atmosphere and a large beach area with chairs and umbrellas. There are also restaurants at the Hilton for food - overpriced, but accessible and decent. If you can get a room at the Hilton for a comparable price to the Normandie, stay at the Hilton. If you can get the Normandie for a significant discount, then it would be worth the savings.I would echo other reviewers that the carpets are stained, the rooms generally clean but look like they're falling into disrepair (cracked walls, dirty windows, etc.). We heard several guests complain about water pressure and temperature but our room was ok. There are no balconies (except for a few rooms on the top floor which they call suites and charge an extra $100/night). The breakfast was disappointing and very overpriced. The internet was slow. It did become expensive taking cabs, but if you're ok taking the bus or walking, the location wasn't too bad.We found a lot of the restaurants overpriced and not that impressive. The Dragonfly in Old San Juan was especially disappointing - food and service were terrible. All in all, we will probably not stay at the Normandie again. If we return to the area, we will probably stay at the Hilton or try our luck staying somewhere else on the island.

<Author>brian_washdc
<Content>Cold showers, slow and unreliable internet - I won't stay here again The Normandie Hotel is aesthetically pleasing -- the lobby is beautiful, and the inner courtyard of the hotel is nice. But the service here is lacking, and the hotel is way overpriced.I stayed here Feb 19-23 on business, choosing this hotel because all the decent hotels in town were already charging more than $300/night. Three out of the four days I was here, the shower was cold. I told the front desk, and they had no response. Also, the high speed internet was slow and unreliable. I tested the connection, and it was between 65kbps - 90 kbps and many times cut out entirely for hours at a time. In order to get work done, I had to walk next door to the Caribe Hilton and camp out in the lobby to use their free WiFi.Fortunately, staying Monday - Friday, I didn't have any troubles with noise from the N Lounge that I'd read about in previous reviews. I would echo other reviewers' comments about the breakfast buffet being disappointing and overpriced at $12. I'd also echo the warnings about the fact that your bill will increase by 20% or more in taxes and fees. My rate here was $250 / night, which then came to $300 with taxes; however, after I voiced my complaints about the cold showers, they discounted my rate 20% for those nights.Having traveled now to Puerto Rico at least 4-5 times, I've come to the conclusion that San Juan's tourism industry is an overpriced racket - it seems as though there's a cartel keeping prices way above market rates in the hotels and major restaurants. However, the real value in Puerto Rico is seen when you travel outside San Juan to the smaller towns, or to Vieques, and stay at the more humble lodgings called Paladares. Buen viaje!

<Author>Tango3
<Content>What did you expect? I just arrived back in the states after a week in Puerto Rico. We stayed at the Normandie for nostalgic reasons. I stayed there in '89 for 3 weeks. Then it was a Raddison Hotel. Considering there had just been a hurricane named Hugo, it was a pleasant stay. This trip was no surprise. I can say that the hotel, was in poorer shape than it was then. However, the room was clean. There were slight older stains on a couple of ceiling tiles, and the carpet was old and a little worn. But the room, linens, furnishings, and bathroom were clean. Considering the structure was built in 1939, these things were to be expected. If you are looking for a super-chic 5 star hotel with fine european linens, this is not the place. We do not set a high standard. If you want a place that is clean, comfortable and practical, this is the place. The in-house food, and room service is over-priced. The Subway Sandwich Shop is across the street. Great for budget traveling. Budget Rental maintains an office at the hotel. Very convenient and recommended as a way to get out and enjoy the island away from San Juan. The cable TV, stereo, and in-room safe were great. This is a very old building that has withstood alot over the years. There is a decent public beach called Escambrone within a short walking distance. The private beach for the hotel is small and void of any tables or other beach ammenities. However, it is a great place to enjoy the warm Atlantic waters. The Escambrone Beach is better equipped and very accessible. The locals use it extensively on weekends, but it was lightly occupied during the week. Old San Juan is a 20 minute walk. There are some hills to climb. It is truly the best way to see all that the city offers.The Cristobal and El Morro Forts are amazing. Lots of stairs and ramps. The entry fee for the forts is $3.00. If you go on Valentine's Day, it's free. It is the park's anniversary.If you travel for the 5 star hotel experience, this is not the place. If you need a clean place to retire for the evening, watch a little TV, and rest up between the other activities and places, then this is for you. The traveler who is independent, self-sufficient, and watches their expenses, can do well here. There could be some service improvement, but as stated above, an independent, self sufficient traveler, would do well at The Normandie. Cab fare is $19-20.00 one way from the airport. For areas around the city of Old San Juan, the fare is $10.00. These are set fares. Cab fares are rated by Tourist zones. The only variable is the number of luggage pieces.

<Author>BonnieAtlanta
<Content>Not Bad This was my birthday trip and after getting a good price from Priceline I was worried about what to expect after reading the reviews on Tripadvisor. Customer service was excellent. The rooms are spacious , but the carpet in the hallways need good cleaning. From reading previous reviews I stayed on the 5th floor so I did not hear the music from the lounges at night. When I went down to the third floor to the exercise room ,you were able to hear the music and it is loud.The hotel resturant has a special three course dinner from 5:00 P.M. to 7:00 P.M. for $19.95 and the food was very tasty. The hotel next door, the Hilton ,have several resturants but they are a bit pricey especially Morton Steakhouse. There is a Subway sandwich shop if you want something simple. I went to Old San Juan one day by public transportation for 50cents. You can catch the bus down the block across the street and it brings you back the same place. If you take a taxicab it will charge you $10.00 to go and $10.00 to come back. If you are a walker when you come out the hotel front door make a right and you can walk to a beach park . If you are a true walker you can take the same path to Old San Juan ,but it gets hot quick and you must start out early in the morning. I did it myself it is over 2 miles.There is an additonal municipal fee and hotel tariff of $21.00 per day added to your stay that is not told to you on check in but I had read about it in one the previous reviews on tripadvisor so it was not a shock. There is a computer room ,free of charge to use in the lobby in a separate room .They will offer to charge you $10.00 for an internet chord at the front desk to use your computer in your room.I personally will stay here again.

<Author>DCtraveler06
<Content>Affordable but out of the way... We just returned from a Thanksgiving trip to San Juan, Puerto Rico and stayed at the Normandie Hotel. All in all, I would say that the accommodations were fine. The room was clean, housekeeping was very considerate, and the hotel staff was very helpful generally. A couple of warnings about the hotel. It's in an area called Puerta de Tierra right between Old San Juan and Condado. There isn't much within walking distance to the hotel, except for the Caribe Hilton, a Subway restaurant right across the street, and Escambron, a restaurant that serves local fare about a 3 minute walk away. As such, you are in close proximity to two very nice areas but don't really get the benefits of staying in either. Cab fare from the hotel to Old San Juan was $10. I'm not sure about the cab fare to Condado because we generally just walked across the bridge. Except for the beach at the Caribe Hilton, every other beach that we saw was a public beach. The beach near the hotel (not the little area behind the hotel but the area behind Escambron Restaurant) is pretty decent and will serve your most basic beach needs. The nicest beach that we went to in the area was in Isla Verde, which was a $19 cab ride from the hotel (not the one near the Ritz Carlton...barf). You probably notice a pattern here! Lots of cabs! You can also take the bus to many areas but it's not terribly convenient.But I digress. Back to the hotel. The hotel has a bar on the second floor called the N-Lounge. The music is unbelievably loud. We were on the fifth floor and at one point during the night, our walls began to shake! I think that someone must have complained b/c they eventually turned the music down. Also, the food in the restaurant downstairs was pretty good (except for an overpriced Thanksgiving holiday buffet). Finally, be aware that San Juan charges a municipal tax of $5/person per day. I thought that I had paid all relevant taxes when I made my reservation only to find that I had to pay an additional fee when I checked out. (i was not advised of this fee in advance and was not pleased). All in all, the Normandie hotel was fine, but I would not stay there again. I would opt for a hotel in Old San Juan instead. With cabs and the traveling time, the price differential is probably worth it. Oh, by the way, make sure you check out this restaurant called Cafe Annapola in Old San Juan. It's along the wall between San Cristobal and El Morro. The food was delicious and the view is amazing!  
<Date>Nov 28, 2006

<Author>CaGlobeTreker
<Content>Great time, friendly staff We stayed during Thanksgiving week. The Staff was courteous, friendly and very helpful. Loved the decor. I wasn't too impressed with the eating facilities or continental breakfast but that was easily overcome by visiting the Caribe Hilton next door. The food was good but just not much variety. The N-Lounge bar is quite nice but only open Thurs _ Sat. although the Atrium bar is open 24 hrs and very comfortable. We didn't make use of the fitness facilities or the Spa. The Spa seemed kind of pricey for the services offered.In the room literature they claim $5.00 for extra coffee packs but that proved to be false in our case. Wireless internet worked very well. Satellite or cable TV have many channels and about half were in english. The room was fairly large (compared to hotels in other countries I have visited, and even some in the US) , divided into an entry/writing area, bedroom/TV room and a sun room. The bathroom was good sized and the only complaint I had there was the water was not as hot as I prefer. It wasn't cold but just a little bit above what I would call warm. A few stains ( not too noticable) on the hallway carpets but I suppose to be expected from a hotel built in '46 or something like that. The pool area was vary nice but hardly used as well as the beach area. We spend most of our time enjoying the facilities at the Hilton next door. The Normandie also offered a substantial discount for AAA members. The location was good. Right between Old Town San Juan and Conado and the casinos. Walking distance to each or ride the A31 bus($.75 p/p) or a fairly cheap and quick taxi ride ($10-12 around town, $19 to the airport) A budget rent a car facility inside the lobby, good service there also. I would recommend this hotel and plan to say again on my next trio to PR. It's not full out luxury but is very unique and well worth the stay unless you have money to burn.

<Author>alexander123
<Content>Perfect Medium Its quite apparent that the Normandie has seen better days, but its better for all that faded glory. The Art Deco architecture is certainly nice--distinguishing amongst the glut of high-end resorts crowding the shoreline of Condado and Isla Verde. The Public areas are the most impressive, while the rooms remain pretty standard--but large and well appointed.The staff were all very helpful: letting us into our room early on our arrival, and keeping our luggage after checkout while we ran around before our flight. My only complaint was the incredibly--almost comically poor--timing of housekeeping to come to our room. In one instance trying to enter our room at 10am, despite a deadbolt, a Do Not Disturb sign, and the hysterical yelling of a young couple as we hurredly threw on our clohes...which I guess you can look at as the houskeeping staff's dedication to their job, if nothing else.Avoid: room service (food is mediocre and overpriced), the cheesy club on the second floor on weekends (cheesy house music and cheesy folks populating the bar), and taking cabs. Do: Take the bus. There's a bus stop right near the hotel (across a busy street, but still) and you can get anywhere in Old San Juan and Condado area for 50 cents. Overall, the location is a huge plus: you can walk to Condado Beaches in 10 minutes, and hop on a bus and be in Old San Juan within 5.In a nutshell: a good, reasonably priced hotel, with nice details, and a great location.

<Author>utqiagvik
<Content>OK ... if you REALLY love Art Deco! My friend and I stayed at the Normandie for five nights in mid-August. This was my second trip to PR, and having stayed at the neighboring Caribe Hilton before (and having walked over to the Normandie and been really impressed by the gorgeous lobby) I decided to book our stay for this second trip at the Normandie, since I really love Art Deco, and since they offered a great rate of $130+tax a night. When checking in I made sure I asked for a room AWAY from the N Lounge (since many other reviewers here have recommended that) ... the check-in lady seemed amused/surprised, but she gave us one nevertheless.Well, what I realized upon staying here is that 99% of the hotel's charm lies in its magnificent exterior and its amazing public areas (the aforementioned lobby and the very unusually-shaped pool). The room itself was a disappointment. Keep in mind the rooms with King beds (like the one we had), which are all located at either ends of the building, are much smaller than the ones with two double beds which are all located in the middle portion of the building, although if you ask for one in the rear of the building the sea-view is much better. There were stains on the walls (especially in the bathroom), the ceilings and the whole bathroom itself were very institutional (ugly and unimaginative, as if all the class and style visible in the lobby area somehow disappeared when one got into the bathroom or looked at the bedroom ceiling). Housekeeping was also hit-or-miss (bottled water some days, none on others, only one coffee pack, and a very distasteful If you need more coffee, let housekeeping know and we'll add $5 to your room charge!). There were also no washcloths in the bathroom, only bath towels and hand towels. The bed looked comfortable, but actually was not very (it was soft but strangely unsupportive). The separate nook for the desk was nice (unusual), and the oversized desk as well as the TV counter were magnificent pieces of modern, Scandinavian-style furniture. A two-seater couch would have been nice to have in addition, especially by the window (they just provided a single-seater).The BIGGEST disappointment however was the lack of a balcony (unless you rent one of the very few and VERY expensive executive-level suites). I applaud the hotel designers for imaginatively designing it to reflect the spirit of an ocean liner, but didn't those have balconies? What's the point of a seaside hotel if there is no place to sit out in private with a friend and enjoy the view and breeze?The other gripe I had was that, while the hotel lobby cafe was extremely overpriced (which is reasonable, given how beautiful the surroundings are and how tasty the food is), but there were NO budget ($25pp) eating options within walking distance except the Subway restaurant. The Condado and Old San Juan areas are much better in this regard, and that's where one had to go to (and pay the to-and-fro cab fare) in order to get meals that did not cost a minimum of $100 for two people.But all said and done, I did not regret my choosing to stay here, because after all, it is a one-of-a-kind building (an absolute Art Deco treasure) with very intriguing history, and it's the kind of place any Art Deco lover ought to stay in at least once. But ONCE is really the keyword for me. I don't think I will stay here again, because when I vacation in a tropical seaside location I absolutely MUST have a balcony, even if it is just a small one. I also need the option of having local restaurants nearby to provide an alternative to expensive in-hotel food.Tip: Actually, having traveled to PR, St. Thomas, and St. Croix, I must say that beach-front hotel rooms are surprisingly cheaper in the US Virgin Islands than they are in PR, even though the latter have a reputation of being more upmarket. But then the biggest reason for me to visit PR is for the people ... simply among the friendliest and most cheerful people I have met in all my travels. Places like USVI and Jamaica don't come anywhere close in terms of friendliness and hospitality to PR, which is why I will visit this beautiful island again and again, if I can...  
<Date>Sep 9, 2006

<Author>nycqt25
<Content>Great Hotel, Helpful Staff My friend and I (two 20 something girls from NYC) booked our trip for Labor Day weekend. We stayed for 4 nights. From the moment we arrived at the hotel, the staff was friendly and helpful. They suggested restaurants, shopping and booked our tours of the rainforest (El Yunque) and Old San Juan. The doormen were polite and always quick to ask if we needed a taxi. PROS: Beautiful hotel; stylish, modern rooms; refrigerator, cable tv, and safe in the room. Hotel spa with hot tub that I luxuriated in while awaiting my massage. Hotel shop with lots of candy, soda, etc. Great location; it's between Old San Juan and Condado; and behind the hotel is Escambron Beach. The beach is literally behind the hotel and to the left. (takes less than 2 min to walk; i walked there each day in my suit  flip flops; hotel has special exit at rear for the beach) So I don't know what the other reviewers are complaining about. There's a great beach nearby, the hotel just doesn't have it's own personal beach. It's also a 5 min. taxi ride to Old San Juan ($10) and close to a restarant on the beach (2 min walk) and the restaurants in the Hilton Hotel which is just next door.CONS: Most of the exercise equipment was broken. My friend got her eyebrows waxed in the spa and it looked terrible. The handle on the bathroom door and the shower lever fell of repeatedly. The hotel shop was ridiculously overpriced. A can of Sprite was $2.00! When they booked our tours, they told us they ended at 2:30PM when they really ended at 4:30PM, which pissed us off b/c we wouldn't have taken more than one if we'd known they would take up our whole day. The 24/hr hotel restaurant was super expensive and had a limited menu. We ordered room service, a $13 plate of shrimp appetizer...ended up costing $26.00 with tax, delivery fee, plus predetermined gratuity! And there were only 3 shrimp on the plate! What a rip off! And they don't even have ice cream in the hotel! ;-) Also of all the restaurants that are supposed to be in the hotel, only 1 of them were open the whole time we were there. And the worst part: the body pillow on our bed smelled like urine!!!!Overall: As much as I've complained, it was still a good experience. Our room was clean, for the most part and the staff was helpful. We also liked the location.

<Author>babymeeshy
<Content>First Trip to PR...definitely not the last I booked a last minute 4-day trip with my boyfriend; so, the rate was not at all unreasonable. When we arrived on a Thurs., we immediately found a white cab to take us to the hotel for about 10 or 11 USD. Since this was short a trip, our main concern was just to get a great tan! And just about every morning, we laid out at the Blue Flag beach El Escambron just a 2-5 minute walk away. It was absolutely gorgeous, but my bf did complain that it is a family beach and that man-made rocks blocked the waves. It never rained for more than 5 minutes. Anywho, the Normandie Hotel is very nice, but the evening reception is unfriendly/unhelpful. My bf found that we got most of our useful info from the bellhops and the budget rent-a car agent across from the front desk. We were originally assigned to a 2nd floor room next to the N lounge, and I had requested a new floor but the receptionists threatened to charge an extra 40 bucks or so per night. Luckily when we tried the room key, it wasn't working and they gave us a room on the 5th floor, which had a great view of the ocean and the El Caribe Hilton next door. The room was cleaned every day by housekeeping. The room was comfortable, and more or less we had no complaints. Because of the proximity, we took the local bus to Old San Juan every day to eat and shop. The food was surprisingly expensive, but i guess they're catering to tourists after all. We did make it to Pamela's at Numero Uno guesthouse in Ocean Park for dinner, which was hands-down the BEST meal we had on the island. Another major highlight was a a tour with Eco-Action tours to Fajardo to swim with the glowing plankton. The tour guide, Peter, picked us up from the hotel for a 40 min ride to Fajardo. He and 2 others led a group of about 20 to the biobay. It was pretty stinky but the experience was well worth it. I would definitely recommend PR for some RR. Would I stay at the Normandie again? Maybe. It is very close to Old San Juan and a short cab ride away from New San Juan. The only thing was that not much is around there but the beach. The food in the hotel was generally overpriced with small portions, but we did like the night server at the Cafe, who was super nice and helpful but he was the only staff there who was taking care of the cafe and room service; so service tended to be slow. All in all an enjoyable stay but much too short!!!

<Author>curlyloxx
<Content>Classy, Art Deco and definitely out of an Ikea catalogue! My boyfriend and I stayed at the Normandie during a much needed weekend trip to Puerto Rico. Upon reading the reviews, I didn't expect much (especially of the beach) but the pictures that were posted of the hotel, to me, showed a beautiful hotel. When we got there, I must admit, I was impressed. The hotel (just like the pictures dictated) was beautiful. The foyer was very trendy... the breakfast area which also doubles as the lounge was very retro-looking, very hip and modern with leather chairs and the most beautiful artwork... the suite was something out of an Ikea catalogue and even the bed was very comfortable.... not to mention, the architecture of the hotel is beautiful, very art deco era... As reported, the parking was $10/night... we parked there for the first night, then street parked across the street for the duration of our stay. The beach (also reported by others) was a dump. I glimpsed it out of the top floor of the hotel and I couldn't believe they had the nerve to even call it a beach! Anyhow, because I knew this, I planned different excursions to several beaches on the island including Playa Flamenco which was rated as one of the best beaches in the world by Conde Nast. Check it out if you get a chance... you have to take a ferry to get to the island of Culebra where the beach is situated, but it's well worth it! Other than that, the only problem we had occured the day we were leaving. In the morning as we were packing our bags, the toilet all of a sudden flushed... and it didn't stop flushing... it flushed over and over for about an hour and a half until we checked out. Also, the bathrooms, aren't as modern looking as the room, but it did the job and wasn't dirty. Just be sure to keep the window open while showering as there is no fan system in the bathroom.I rated the hotel 4 stars (above average) cause I felt it definitely was above average. The continental breakfast was fresh and there was a variety of things to eat including fresh fruit, pastries, bagels and muffins. I didn't really need to talk to the staff until check-out so I didn't have a problem with them... my room was always made up when I got back from excursions... I never experienced the sound problems most complain of (I stayed on the fourth floor)... overall, I had a great experience and would definitely go back should I find myself on a weekend trip to Puerto Rico!  
<Date>Aug 14, 2006

<Author>Hay_Papito
<Content>Nice for a first trip to San Juan Recently traveled to San Juan with my girlfriend for a few days of relaxation and fun. The initial room that we were put in had a good view but the A/C in the room was not working well and it was very warm. Maintenance responded to the room and tried to reset the A/C but to no avail. We contacted the on duty manager and we were put in another room on the third floor. The first room also had a door that led to a utility room, not standard for most hotel rooms. The room that we were moved to was very nice except the shower leaked. Overall the room was quite spacious and the bed was large and comfortable. The room was clean and with a good view of the surrounding area. The pool was nice and clean, room service was adequate and the workout room was pretty small but with a great view. The hotel did not appear in disrepair but could use some beautification to make it a bit more aesthetically pleasing. We ate a late lunch at the hotel bar and the service was slow but the food was good. There appeared to be a lot of staff on scene and they were all friendly and eager to assist. The hotel is good place for a romantic getaway especially if you are with good company but if you want it quiet ask for a room close to the pool as the club on the second floor gets hopping on the weekends. One tip is not to buy items from the shop in the hotel (large bottle of water = $4.50) there is a little market just down the street across from the Hilton that has bottled water, gatorade, sodas and snacks for a much more reasonable price. Go to the Normandie if you want a HUGE clean room at a good price. I would also check out the Hilton if I was looking to stay in that part of town though, huge swimming pool, private beach and several restaurants and a Starbucks on their property.
