<Content>bad pool and No beach I went to San Juan to visit a friend from college and brought my mother along expecting her to be able to hang out at the pool and beach. The pool was allright.. a little dirty and not very modern. The beach that was promised was barely a beach at all. there was about 5 feet of sand until you reached the water and the area was always filled with scuba divers from a very nearby scuba school. It is hard for me to say how I liked the room we stayed in. You walk in and there is a small room with nothing in it except a desk and one light, then through a doorway is the bedroom with two queen sized beds and a tv. The beds were VERY comfortable and soft and the tv was a good size also. The problem was, one bed was only a foot away from the far wall which had the door to the bathroom. It was very cramped and hard for my mother to get in and out of that area. The room also only had one small light so it was very dark in the mornings and evenings when the light wasn't coming in through the windows. At night (i only know of the weekends) there are parties in all of the banquet roooms of the hotel and in the Lounge there is a bar and dancing (very fun if you are 25-35ish). It starts early and ends late... which made it hard for my mother to sleep at night.I would recommend this hotel if you are coming to San Juan on business and if you are not a light sleeper

<Content>Unacceptable The Normandie is a hotel that has survived well past its time. They were not able to provide a non-smoking room even though reservations were made well in advance. The room suffered from lingering odor of smoke, the shower handle fell off, the cold water ceased working leaving scalding hot water only, the key cards constantly failed and had to be recoded three times. And the front desk service was indifferent. Credit does go to the maid and concierge for reasonably good service. The wireless and wired internet service did not work in the room, at least in our room. I had to sit in the lounge area to get usable reception. Overall, the 4 day stay was 4 days too long. It appears to be surrounded by bigger and better hotels, Caribe Hilton,etc. There are two signs in front of the hotel; one lists valet parking for $5.00 and the other for $15.00, $15.00 for valet parking? The food was not very satisfying in the lounge restaurant. A turkey/cheese wrap consisted of 80% wrap skin, one slice of turkey and one slice of cheese but more important, well overpriced and not worth the money. We would have probably done better at the Subway across the street. Finally, on the last evening, during the night, a strong odor seeped into the room that was similar to an open septic tank for several minutes. Go somewhere else.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>I liked it, but... A colleague and I who are both travel agents stayed at the Normandie the weekend of June 9th, Friday and Saturday evenings recently and I thought I'd offer a quick review.Although we had made the reservation about 2 weeks in advance, to avoid any snags I had faxed the hotel the week before our stay to alert them to the fact that we would not be arriving at the hotel until around 3am due to our late flight and it was imperative that we have a room with 2 beds.As you can imagine, it was the usual story:our room had a king bed and due to the hotel being full, there was nothing available with 2 beds. After explaining that this was unacceptable, and pointing out the fact that we were both travel agents coming to look at the property since neither of us had stayed there before, she finally 'found' a room with 2 double beds, but warned us that it was not remodeled or renovated. At that point, after working a full day and flying 3 1/2 hours from Newark, as long as the room had 2 beds, we were fine. Even the view was unimportant to us, all we wanted to do was sleep!We were given room 605, which must be one of those save for the overflow-don't give this room unless the hotel is desperate kind of rooms. When she said it was not remodeled, she was being kind!Neverless, it was relatively clean and although the beds were old, the linens were clean and beds were comfortable.The next morning we left the room before 9am and put the 'please clean room' sign on the door handle. Let me follow up by saying that there are only a few guest rooms on the 6th floor as it's mostly meeting rooms and the banquet area, etc.Needless to say, we returned to our room after 1pm to find the maid had not been there yet. I was planning on calling down to the front desk to let them know since I presumed it was possible the housekeeping was not aware anyone was staying in it, being an overflow room.It was then I discovered the room had no telephone!That was definitely the last straw so we went down to the front desk and was told this time by a different agent that she would have to get the manager, nothing else was available, room-wise.Although he was pleasant, he was rather standoffish and cool and he never once made any apology or offered any explanations. However, we were moved to the 7th floor in a newly renovated room with 2 doubles. It was like night and day! Although we did not have an ocean view nor balcony, the room was great and we felt that the hotel did the right thing by moving us and we were pleased and satisfied with the room.I have been to Puerto Rico many times and have stayed in various areas around the island. The location of the Normandie is not bad, adjacent to the Caribe Hilton and a $10 cab ride to the Condado. If you're a walker, the stroll to Old San Juan is about 35-45 minutes, but quite pleasant if it's not a really humid day....The pool was small, but not overly crowded or noisy like the pool at the Hilton. The restaurant in the lobby serves breakfast and lunch and is quite reasonably priced with decent food. As other reviewers have said, the beach is an afterthought, but there is a better public beach in the state park, just west of the property.The Caribe Hilton was strict about asking if you were staying at their hotel, so using their beach was out, but I have a feeling if it were a less busy weekend or perhaps a weekday, it would've been possible.Would I stay here again? Maybe. Granted, being travel agents, we were paying a good rate. I just was a bit perplexed that since my colleague and I are in travel industry and can either send the hotel clients or dissuade people from staying there, we were perplexed that the hotel did not do a bit more to 'impress' us or at least offer an apology. I have a feeling that based on many earlier reviews, the management is a bit jaded when it comes to complaints since it seems like they must get them quite often.I would, however, be reluctant to recommend the hotel to clients for fear that they would have a similar experience that would reflect poorly upon myself and my agency.If the hotel would just do themselves a favor and renovate the few rooms that still aren't finished I would feel much more comfortable sending them business.Also, customer service needs some serious improvement as I believe no matter what rate you are paying or what venue you've booked through-either travel agent, Priceline, Expedia, hotel website, etc you should still try to accommodate your guests and make sure they're happy. My review would've been 4 of 5 if it hadn't been for the hotels disinterest and lack of professionalism dealing with guest complaints!A few quick points-Get a room on the 7th floor...the hallways on some of the other floors are unusually dark and drab, but the top floor is under the skylight and is well-lit and pleasant.The gift shop in hotel is overpriced for usual things like bottled water, soda, snacks, etc (but then again, do you know many cheap gift shops at hotels?).Do yourself a favor and pick up supplies outside at one of the many small markets or Walgreens since most of the rooms have a fridge and you can easily store drinks, etcIf you do have a complaint, be firm, but pleasant. I'm sure if we were aggressive and rude in voicing our gripes, we would still be in that crappy unrenovated room!

<Content>Loved Puerto Rico/Hotel ok I just returned from my trip to Puerto Rico. I spent all my time there- from lunches, beach time, pool time to drinks at their swim up bar. It is more welcoming.Best things to Do: El Yunque Rainforest Trip and also Kayaking at night at the lagoon in Fajardo! So much fun..I booked with A and B Tours. they were great. ask fo rHector, he was our tour guide and we loved him.

<Author>Perki
<Content>Beware - Some rooms are better than others I booked this hotel for a one night stay, using Hotwire as we decided to take a cruise just 3 1/2 weeks before the departure date so I knew it was going to be hard to find a hotel last minute as many stay in San Juan a day or two pre-cruise so the city is usually quite booked up. That being said once I was booked with Normandie Hotel the reservation said to contact the hotel directly for any further help or questions. 3 days before we arrived I called and confirmed our reservation, notified them that we would be late arrivals as our flight didn't land til almost 8pm and requested a King size bed as my huband is a larger guy and I didn't want to spend the 1st night of our Anniversary vacation in separate beds - the two of us would never fit in a standard double bed. I was told that all would be noted in their system on our reservation, not a problem. While waiting for our connecting flight from Miami to San Juan I again called to confirm late arrival and King bed and was told that our reservation did show that and that all would be in order when we arrived later that day. Well we arrived and went to the first room, #606 and it was 2 double beds. It was hard to see as the lights only worked in the bathroom just as you entered the room, the ones in the sleeping area weren't working and there wasn't a phone in the room either - both of which puzzled the luggage steward that was following us with our bags. From what I could see in the dark this room's decor didn't even remotely resemble the pictures from any of the travel sites for this hotel - flowery bedspread kind of maybe and real dark carpet? Certainly not art deco and the room was very musty smelling and damp feeling. So we went back to the front desk and I explained our dismay and explained my 2 previous conversations with persons from their hotel. The desk clerk said that with Hotwire we could receive a double or a king and I said I understand and that is why I called to notify I needed a King so they could be certain to accomodate us. They swapped us over to room #211 and lo and behold if it wasn't identical to the one in all the travel site pictures - cool colors on the walls, nice bedding, cool airconditioning and no musty smell, etc. So I guess the moral of the story is, if you don't book direct and use a price hunting website some hotels feel they can give you their worst room and you have no reason for disappointment, but I feel if they have these different rooms they need to show them all on the websites so you know the range of what is possible to get so one can make and educated decision on if they want to take a chance to get stuck with a room like that. All I had was a picture of a gorgeous room and believed they all looked like that why would I expect otherwise? So it worked out for us but may not for others so just so you know - all the rooms are NOT as nice as the ones in their picture. Also I think they have put money into the main areas of the hotel which do look nice but that one room #606 I saw was 2 steps down in quality from what the rest of the hotel looked like - sad. Would I stay here again, maybe, but I would have to be certain that I could get a room identical to #211 and not #606, if they couldn't guarantee me that, then no I would not chance it with a room such as #606 it was sub-par.Also as another person noted above the night we stayed there was a Quincinera (coming of age latin party, usually 15yrs old) so there were hundreds of teens running around and loud music, especially up on the 6th floor by the 1st room they had us going into. There was no way we could have gotten any sleep that night so we are lucky they moved us to #211. I don't know if there is any way to know this when booking, maybe one could ask when making a reservation, but their events centers are mixed in with the rooms not on the ground floor tucked in corner so as to not disturbed ones sleep - it is a hotel which is what most people want is a good nights rest. Also 1 of the central elevators was not working at all and the teens pretty much kept the other one tied up riding up and down and cramming many bodies in so we actually used a back elevator not usually used for guests, but it was more comfortable and reliable so suited me fine.San Juan is such an odd place to find a decent hotel at a decent price. We paid almost $150 with all taxes and everything which I do not consider cheap and this hotel's rooms usually run over $200/nt so I am glad I paid what I did. Next time I think I'll try the Carib Hilton or another better known place as this place isn't consistent in it's quality.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic hotel! This is a fantastic hotel, and I have previously stayed in MANY hotels in San Juan. I was here for 4 nights for business, and just extended by stay by 2 days (weekend) because I can not bear to leave! They were actually booked for the weekend, but accomodated by request to stay. How do you spell paradise? Beautiful hotel with a trendy South Beach feel to entertain singles, yet I also saw many families who also seemed to be enjoying themselves here. Art deco lobby with a 24 hour bar, great restaurants, and the best was every I time I return to the hotel in the evening, they have aromatic candles burning to welcome you home. Heavenly! The attention to this level of detail is evident throughout the hotel and is why it deserves the high rating I am giving it. Well-staffed and incredibly gracious service, from check-in thru maid service, I have only encountered smiling, helpful faces throughout. The restaurants were excellent (no boring , over-priced hotel food comes out of any of their kitchens). We had our pick of places to go in San Juan and kept finding ourselves coming back to the hotel to eat. There was one lobster pasta dish at their Cru restaurant that all of us raved over, and I think I have to go back and have again! I thought the prices were reasonable for San Juan and esp for the quality you receive. Even breakfast off the menu was innovative, delicious and well-priced i n the typical hotel range. I had a special request for lunch and the kicthen accomodated it beautifully. Not to mention, my room is beyond expectation. It is 3 large rooms, an office area, bedroom and sitting room, with a huge bathroom. The bed is the most comfortable bed I have ever slept on, with plenty of pillows and fine linens on bed and in bath. Gilchrist and Soames toiletries with sea kelp bits add to the luxury. Actually, the whole experience here has been one of a pampered spa. Wireless and/or cable hook up included, so you can do business or stay connected with email so easily. Phillips CD player in room. I feel very spoiled here. Some of the other reviews complained about thin walls and noise. I did not have this problem, but maybe its because the bed is so comfortable I drifted off to such a comfortable sleep! The maids did SUCH a good job cleaning my room every day, again, I haven't seen this kind of attention to detail in such a long time, and I'm a biz traveler who has stayed in some great hotels. They really service you here. Even the gift shop is innovative and fun- and also sells those great candles! I haven't been to the spa yet but am very tempted to give it a try. The pool is much better than I expected, large and with spacious seating capacity. The beach area behind the hotel is small, but as other reviews have said, you can either go to the Caribe Hilton next door or just behind the hotel is a nice public beach. I honestly don't know how you could improve upon this experience, I can't think of a single thing they are missing. They even have a small refrig in the room, along with a safe, etc. Location for me is excellent- you can easily walk across the bridge to Condado strip, or to Old San Juan which is a little further but a short taxi ride away. I find Condado strip/Ashford Ave gets a bit noisy and busy, so being just off of it slightly gives you a more restful yet convenient experience. I stayed here once about 5 years ago and there is a huge difference in what they have done. They have managed to take a big old landmark and somehow made it a boutique hotel with a resort feel. They seem to have a lot of fun events, Mango Mojitos night, an art party, and tonight there is an Afterparty for Puerto Rican High Fashion week! Clearly, this is a San Juan hotel that you will be reading more favorable things about. Other guests seem to be smiling as well, and the whole ambience here is something special. Kudos go out to the management and staff of this wonderful hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Sweet old hotel The Normandie has a charm that I can't quite define. As another reviewer mentioned you can sense the greatness that this hotel once possessed.The hotel was very clean and the staff were friendly but not obtrusive. In fact I had no complaints with any of the service. The bartender and the attendant by the pool were as sweet and friendly as could be without being phony.The room was good sized although the location was not ideal (we overlooked the tennis courts at the spa next door - try and ask for a higher floor more towards the ocean). Everything was clean although showing some minor signs of age (some discolorations of the carpet, etc.) that had no impact on the comfort of the accomodation. The bed and linens were fabulous to sleep on.We did hear the music from a banquet one night but honestly, unless you are super sensitive to sound it isn't difficult to deal with.The pool was impeccably maintained and there was always a peaceful quiet and plenty of space, sun or shade, to rest.True the beach is non-existent but as the park is right there you have the chance to walk to a better beach area or you can also mingle with locals on the weekend. I spent some time watching some local in-line skaters doing tricks off the wall, which was pretty cool.The breakfast is nothing to write home about and is a little pricey. For $19 there is a breakfast buffet at the Caribe Hilton just next door (literally a walk around the corner) that would keep you stuffed all day long. The area has nothing else in the immediate vicinty. You will have to walk the bridge over to Condado to find off property restaurant choices or you can pay the taxi fare to go to Old San Juan or Isla Verde (taxis are quite pricey so be prepared). We wanted to take buses but they are few and far between...although cheap you could be waiting for an hour or more (even though they say they run every 20 minutes).Speaking of the Hilton we had friends there and their room was small compared to ours, although they did have a balcony. The pool and beach there is nice but TERRIBLY crowded and loud.Overall give some consideration to the Normandie. It's a very interesting hotel with a history and charm that will win you over.

<Author>StaceyBorsik
<Content>Puerto Rico was wonderful Normandie was a great hotel to stay at. My trip was for 4 days and 3 nights. The staff was very nice. The location is fantastic! I only was at the hotel to sleep, the pillows are wonderful and the rooms were great. Puerto Rico is full of so many things to do. Old San Juan, just minutes away and a $10 taxi ride. During the day check out the forts plus plenty of shops. Old San Juan is the place for nightlife, great bars and posh restaurants. Check out a great casual bar called NoNo. The hotel concierge Andrew was extremely helpful, ask for him only. If you are going to rent a car, rent it at the Normandie as there is a Budget rent a car on site at the hotel. You can rent a car for $30 a day, by not renting at the airport you don pay the airport surcharge. Parking at the hotel is $10 a nightr just park outside on the curb for free, that what I did. For a great authentic cheap Puerto Rican breakfast or lunch visit La Tropical Cafeteria, it is just across from the hotel to the left of Subway. You have to visit the El Yunque Rain Forest while your in Puerto Rico, youl see gougous waterfalls and magnificent senic views plus cool hiking trails. Make sure you wear shoes with soles, not flip flops as the rain forest is very wet and slick. Bring a plastic poncho if you don want to get wet. Luquillo is a great beach town, you will see rows of kiosks of restaurants, bars  shops. Be sure to eat at Kiosco #2 La Parrilla Bar  Grill Restaurant, the Yuca Rings are delicious, just like onion rings but better, the mahi mahi was wonderful. In Luquillo you can horseback ride on the beach, again wear those shoes, not the flip flops. Travel pass Fajado and go to the Puerto del Rey Marina, it is the largest marina in the Caribbean. That is were you can take an awesome catamaran boat trip all day from 10am-3:30pm. Book with East Island Excursions ----, the astwind II?is a 62?catamaran with glass bottom windows, on board waterslide, lunch is provided and complementary Rum drinks, Pina Coladas, Rum Punch or $2 beers. The boat sails to an island off the coast and provides snorkeling gear for checking out the coral reefs, this excursion is a Must at only $59 per person! Fun for kids and adults! If you like to fish, deep sea fishing is a must. We caught 2 Tunas with Caribbean Outfitters, ----, $525 for a half a day for up to 6 people. Do Not go fishing on the day you leave, do it earlier in the trip so that if you catch fish you can take it to a local restaurant and enjoy it. We couldn find anyone who would pack and ship. After the trip Captain Omar arranged for someone to come out to the marina and filet the fish and we ate raw tuna right there, just like eating sushi! We took some of the fish home that day on the plane in a plastic cooler from Walgreens, the rest we gave to Captain Omar and Axle. Enjoy your trip, Puerto Rico is a wonderful place to vacation. If you want all the comforts of home youl have it or take a step of the beaten path and try something new like a CoCo Frio which is a coconut that you drink the coconut water straight coconut or a Caf con leche, coffee with warm milk, delicious! Again, enjoy the trip, I can wait to go back and check out Rincon on the West side of the island!

<Author>DVPinNYC
<Content>Great hotel, not great location The best part of Normandie is the room. The room had a huge bed and was very clean and modern. The rest of the hotel was not as great. There really is not a beach about a foot of sand and the pool was okay, nothing fancy. The hotel has a small cafe for breakfast, overpriced buns. There is a club and bar in the hotel, but after a walkthrough, the cable TV in the room seemed more appealing. There is a bigger beach near by, walking distance and a park across the street that is nice to walk in. We went next door to the Marriott; they have a beautiful pool (and a Starbucks). They were checking if you were staying there on the weekends, otherwise we were not asked. There is a Subway and other deli/convenient stores nearby. Take the 25 cent bus to Old San Juan, very quick ride. It would be better to stay by the nicer beaches, closer to the airport. We took a long, nauseating bus ride to the beach at the Intercontinental one-day, gorgeous hotel with an amazing pool and beach. One big perk of Normandie is its closeness to Old San Juan, which has a lot of great restaurants and is nice to walk around the streets.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>I had an AWSOME stay!! I've seen several negative reviews but my expreince was nothing but the best. Staff bent over backwards for me. I hate to say it but I was in Puerto Rico for 4 days, and partially due to the rain, and partially due to the wonderful hotel room I had, I didn't get out much. :-) The room service was amazing and I had in-room breakfast, lunch, dinner and late-night several times. The restaurant and the room service food was FAR above my expectations. The wine list is great too. The hotel is on a public beach and the part that comes up to the hotel property is great for swiming but not for laying around -- it's too narrow. On the one day I had sun, I lounged around the pool and then went for a swim at the beach. The colors, the carpeting, everything was thoroughly modern but went well with the art deco architecture. The gift shop was unique as it didn't have the standard cheap/tacky nick-nacks, but gourmet treats and locally designed clothing. Very expensive but it was nice not to find a gift shop full of snow-globes!

<Author>bethannsd
<Content>Interesting mix but overall fine hotel I read many reviews about the Normandie prior to making the reservation, as we were hesitant to stay there with the bad reviews. We were there for a conference at the Caribe Hilton, which is directly next door, and they were sold out. We made reservations with Karla Santiago, who was very helpful and courteous. I called several times prior to our trip to make sure we would have a room (a problem for previous guests per the reviews) as we had booked a jr suite with a king bed. When we arrived, the lobby and hotel appearance was very nice and clean. The service at the front desk was nice and we were told we were upgraded to the 7th floor executive room area. It had a beautiful view but had 2 double beds...which was not what we asked for. The hotel was full and we could not change rooms. The beds were VERY comfy, FYI. The line 1 on the telephone did not work nor did the internet, which is supposed to be free at the hotel. We asked and asked for it to be fixed and the hotel just could not figure it out and our entire week we did not have service. That was disappointing. We rented a car for one day and parked at the hotel for one day only. When we checked out we were billed for 4 days of parking, which was promptly removed by the front desk. Andrew, the concierge/bellman was very helpful and pleasant, and we had a nice stay, other than the bed and internet. The pool is fine and not too small, as others have complained about. The beach is very small, but the Hilton Beach is a 30 second walk away and every one uses it. We had no noise issues that others complained about, but if we were on a lower floor we would have, as the lobby is in the middle of the hotel and completely open and noise is abundant down there at night. The 6th floor has ball rooms and had a large wedding Saturday night, but the noise quieted by 1130 PM, and was no big deal. Initially our room had no hot water, but the maintence man was there in minutes to fix it for us. The housekeeping was good and the food in the restaurant was good, although we only had one breakfast there. Overall, I would stay at the Normadie again, but demand working internet, as that is part of their service. We were too busy to deal with it other than asking every single day for it to be fixed. We were not even offered a free dinner to compensate, which I felt was unprofessional. But the hotel was clean, nice beds, nice linens, nice view, overall good service.

<Author>thegoodlife1000
<Content>Pretty good if you have a quiet room I stayed at the Normandie for 5 nights in mid-March. First the good: The architecture is cool, the lobby bar is funky, the rooms are comfortable, the location is convenient - only a 10 minute bus ride (50 cents)into Old San Juan so even though there's not much wrt good restaurants in the area, it's really easy to go into town every night. The not so good: The first room we were given (Rm 725 - Do not accept this room!) was horribly noisy as everytime a toilet in the hotel was flushed a tank above our heads would shake the room. Also it adjoined an old noisy elevator. We were switched after 2 nights and our second room was much quieter. The service in the hotel was not particularily responsive and we had to keep on reminding the front desk about our concerns to ensure that a new room was found for us. As well, when we first arrived our room safe was locked and we had to call the front desk 6X (and wait 24 hours), before someone unlocked it for us. In spite of these problems, though, I would consider staying here again if I had to go to San Juan for something and the price was right.

<Author>biberbunch
<Content>We thought it was OK A group of four girls made this once in a lifetime trip. I had booked 2 rooms on line. We checked in before the crowd (?), but had to plead for ocean front rooms. We got the LAST (?) ones. Unfortunately, we also had to sleep on king size beds, rather than the 2 separate ones. I can't say the hotel ever seemed full, though. The rooms seemed overpriced, but still on the cheaper end of hotels on that strip.Beds  pillows were fabulous. We did have great housekeeping, and even the sheets were changed every night. (I had dropped a makeup brush one morning, and left a small inconspicous stain. I was pleasantly surprised to come back that evening to find the sheets were fresh.) We stayed on the 3rd floor, overlooking the parking lot and the beach area. I also believe that being so far from the club, we weren't bothered by too much noise. Very disappointed to find out there are no balconies! Photos misled us. You can prop open a little condensation saturated window to feel the breeze on your face. We did have forceful water pressure in the showers (hot), and yes, the toilets took longer to flush-- but what's a few more seconds?? For the little time we spent in the rooms, no one complained, except for no ocean front balconies.Beach is more like a lagoon. Public beach is within walking distance, and it was super. Hilton is next door, so we would walk there for the gift shops, restaurants, Starbucks. We never ate at the Normandie. We even booked our excursions from there.Normandie is the last hotel before Old San Juan. I liked the proximity. You can walk to OSJ, but it is farther than it looks! The 4 of us are quiet, so we enjoyed the quiet location and the family oriented public beach. We used taxis to travel, and that adds up. Those looking to be in the heart of the action (more clubs, casinos, restaurants, etc.) may consider looking a little further east into the Condado. Boring people like us, would probably be satisfied. :-)I'd consider staying here again- with friends. Would not stay here if I were bringing the husband and kids. Not as family friendly.

<Content>This was not a welcoming hotel Without totally ripping the place, I liked the location and the elegance of the structure itself. To the reviewer below: I couldn't have said it any better. Considering that we could have stayed at any hotel, they really tried to advocate that they were doing us a favor. We had prepaid for our room but the Normandie tried to cancel our reservation while we were in transit. They actually made up a story. Catching them in a lie when we arrived, they gave us our room. They admitted to being over-booked however there was no appology or consolation for thier actions. I think we probably did get lucky because we arrived before the rush of guests. Being well-dressed may have helped, who knows?Our room was indeed small but had the vacant fridge which was convenient. I have to say our bed was outstanding. Pleasantly soft with comfortable linens. The room itself was clean and all the general amenities were in place. Others note that this is a noisy hotel but I'm a light sleeper and heard nothing. I have my doubts if they were truthful about being sold out. People who surf: I ended up leaving quiver home because of bad winds but this hotel is right next to Escambron Park. There is also a surf shop across the street called La-8 surfshop as in the 8th bus stop. Convenient if you are travelling with your G/F who doesn't surf and would rather shop. Had the surf delivered, I would have been happy with being in short walking distance to the break, the surfshop and the hotel.I think the building itself is 4 stars but the human content needs reconsidering. We remained cool and understanding throughout our stay and did our best to put the desk problmes behind us but it was very stressful after having dealt with this situation and feeling unwanted. This hotel exercises classic arrogance with limited service and lack-luster hospitality. This is unfortunate because I'm sure its either just a few bad apples spoiling the bunch or poor management making the help look bad. Puerto Ricans are known for being very friendly, accomodating and hard-working people so I'm not sure what looms over the Normandie.

<Author>Maryland20855
<Content>Nice Building, No Services Stayed at the Normandie for 6 nights with a group. The building is very attractive (we are art deco fans), and the room was good-sized. However, this hotel offers no services whatsoever. The room was never vacuumed, barely cleaned, and the towels are thin, threadbare and skimpy. Days Inn caliber. The tub leaked, and the toilet was dirty. They never replaced the in-room coffee. One nice feature is a small refrigerator in each room...but there are only a couple of mini-markets within walking distance to buy anything edible. The hotel has no vending machines and no gift shop, so you can't even get water or a soda on the premises. As for the service - very poor. We asked for a room on a high floor and were given the 2nd floor, though others in the group were on the 6th floor. Heard every word said by people in the adjoining room. The pool was nice but cold. The beach is a joke. My advice - stay in the Condado, and avoid this place until they get some management that cares about service.

<Author>samuelfp
<Content>Great room, beach and pool not so hot Whether you'll like this hotel depends on what you value in a hotel and a little bit of luck. Our room was excellent...very large with a main room with the bed and TV, a second smaller room with a desk, and third small room with a chase lounge. The decor was modern and everything was clean.However, the toilet didn't work properly (had to hold the handle down for 5-10 seconds to make it flush) and the shower was never hot. Over the four days we were there it varied from very warm to room temperature. Also, when we first arrived the power was out in the hotel. It seems they have their own generators rather than getting power from the grid and, from reading other reviews it seems this is not the first time this happened.We were at the far end of the hotel, away from the N Lounge so we didn't have any problems with noise, but we could see how if you got a room nearby that would be a major headache.The pool area was ok. It felt very urban though, with lots of concrete and not many trees. The beach area was a definite negative. If you want to stay at a hotel with nice beach access don't pick this one. If you do stay here you can just walk over to the Hilton Caribe next door and use their beach access.Service was OK. One one occassion the concierge was happy to call to make a restaurant reservation for us. Another time when we asked if he knew if a particular restaurant was open on a Monday night he said I think so rather than offering to call...it turned out to be closed.From what I've read it seems like the rooms here are nicer than those at the Hilton Caribe or El San Juan, but the beach and pool area is definitely sub-par. Where you decide to stay depends on what you value most.

<Content>Simply Awful My new husband and I booked our trip through expedia, and for the last leg of our honeymoon, had reserved a junior suite at the Normandie . However, room service is terrible, and takes forever.We would never stay in this hotel again, and would warn others, that under the skin of this lovely-to-look-at hotel, is almost nothing good, which is truly a shame.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent for the price We paid $97/night for this place through Hotwire. Was a bit disturbed by the numerous bad reviews and steeled myself for something horrible. Turned out to be a pretty good place.The room was lovely, spacious, airy, we had a partial ocean view. My boyfriend didn't care for the art deco but I found it charming. He was amused by the ocean liner theme. Comfortable bed, great shower (hot and high pressure). Free Internet tho it took them a couple hours to get us a hookup after we called and asked why it wasn't working. Didn't take advantage of any of the hotel ameneties, preferring to walk across the street to the Subway and the little local cuisine place, there's a liquor store there where I got cheaper beer too. (Interesting note - it's apparently illegal to walk around with an open container in PR, which is why if you buy a beer and ask to have it opened, they'll almost always pour it into a cup, tho a couple times I walked by police while drinking beer from a cup and nothing was said to me).Anyhow. The people in the most part were amiable, doors would be opened for me, etc. Yes the location is out of the way but this is good! Given that PR is such a noisy late-night city and there is a bus stop very close to the hotel. Tried to get a key to the workout room but was told it was being renovated (didn't investigate to find out more).There was visible wear, chipped tile in the bathroom, water stained ceiling partitions; this really didn't bother us.We did have noise problems, it was more of a reverberation in the wall and if I walked out into the hallway, it wasn't as loud! The only thing I could figure was we were directly above the club and the noise was coming up through the wall. Another night there was a noisy party but both times the noise didn't last too terribly late, midnightish or so.For $97/night I thought it was an excellent value (by PR standards). Really nice place to hang around for a couple days pre-cruise.

<Content>Do NOT stay here if you plan to sleep before 1 AM The rooms were fine, but the service at this hotel was TERRIBLE. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Poor Service Mars Overall Experience Stayed at Normandie for 4 nights between Christmas and New Year's. Pros were: well-decorated, modern, clean, and spacious room. People were generally friendly. Convenient location between Old San Juan and Condado - $10 cab ride to either area. Sleek, modern philippe stark wannabe. Quiet during the day.Cons were: noisy (thin walls. we were woken by noise of other guests / music from banquet room on 2 of 4 nights), unresponsive/indifferent service (e.g. were not given breakfast tickets and it took a couple of requests and a few hours before they brought us any; asked for help finding rental car and concierge promised to call back but never did despite 2 requests, concierge desk overall of little value), very slow lines at front desk (one person manning it usually, or two with one person just standing there) - led to waits even to get the key to the treadmill in the fitness room (why they make you sign in for it at the front desk on another floor on other end of hotel is beyond me). Tiny fitness center with bad antiseptic smell. Also (pet peeve) no pay-per-view movies despite nice TV and CD player in the room. Other rooms looked sort of dark (we had 7th/top floor room). Overall, not a bad value. We paid $180 per night during high season, and given it was our first visit to San Juan we got to check out most areas from this central location. Pool and beach area are dumpy, but guests often use Hilton beach area next door since all beaches are by law public.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Three Cheers to the Normandie! I've never written a review before, but my great stay at the Normandie is worth sharing...I travel to PR a lot for business and know that the Normandie is one of the most historic and architecturally-distinctive (art deco) properties on the Island. After a period of disrepair, another period of a really bad renovation (horrible dark colors), the hotel has finally gotten it right (with its current new owners/management). The hotel is light and airy, with beautiful art deco decor and all the modern amenities you'd want in a boutique hotel. I ended up staying here because my reservation was lost at the Sheraton Old San Juan (stay away from there, this is the second time they pulled that on me so they clearly just don't want my business as a frequent business traveler to the Island).Anyway, the staff at the Normandie welcomed me late at night with a room upgrade and complimentary breakfast for my troubles (which were caused by the other hotel). The welcoming, attentive and helpful staff really seem to care about guest needs (i.e., explaining Internet set-up, approaching me at check out to see if I need a cab, offering a to-go cup for my coffee at breakfast when my meeting plans changed and I had to run off, etc.). My room was oversized, with a big desk and free wi-fi service so that I could work easily -- all the while overlooking the ocean (gorgeous sunrise view!). As a boutique property, they seem to be serving the needs of visitors well. 24 hour food service (good, though basic), a cocktail lounge, (tiny) fitness center and beautifully redone pool area (also art deco). Not much of a beach, and to be honest, you've got to take a cab to Old San Juan and other area attractions/nightlife/casinos, etc. But if you're in PR for business or just passing through to head out on a cruise, etc. this is a perfect place to stay (the hotel is shaped like a ship!). Loved it and can't wait to go back.  
<Date>Jul 17, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Unique beauty! Great consierge staff! Okay, so my husband and I are not the types who crave luxury but we were so spoiled by this place, and for a reasonable rate, that we may have lost our ability to accept good enough hotels for the same price. The architecture is unique, the color scheme and design are very soothing, cool colors with classic art deco furniture. Lots of great lighting. The rooms are huge: a medium-sized area with a phone, large bedroom and a smaller cozy sitting area with a love seat for a closer view of the ocean. The front desk were terrific and made every effort to accomodate us in so many ways. They even let us check-in and out based on our needs. So the downsides are, there are some very young staff in the lounge area who are slow and casual about providing service--but there is a very energetic and generous 30?-something bartender who gave us wonderfully stiff, larger than average, drinks and genuine hospitality. Also, if you need to workout, expect to swim or run along the ocean, the work-out area is aniquated and rusty. But they are in the process of renovating it so maybe in the next year it will be up and running. I love this place. --Boston couple

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic Hotel! I stayed in a Jr. Suite from June 29-July 2 of 2005 with a friend. We were equally struck by the beauty of the hotel lobby area and we were hoping that the rooms were similarly fashionable. The room exceeded our expectations. It was something straight out of a West Elm catalog. Very complimentary cool colors (white, taupe, seafoam), two comfortable beds, a small dressing room or entertainment area with a couch and two ottomans that could double as tables, and a desk sitting area. Four rooms including the bathroom! Beautiful! Well cleaned everyday (even though the cleaning lady came a bit early in the morning for us, 9:30am). There are no negatives about the room or our stay. The N Lounge was hopping on Friday and Saturday night. Even though we stayed on the same floor as the lounge, we could hear nothing! This is the sign of a well constructed building. I intend to stay here again on my next visit. Oh! If you are not impressed by the smallish strip of beach behind hotel, feel free to use any of the other hotels' beach space. The Caribe Hotel next door may hassle you, but legally (and I verified this with a Puerto Rican attorney) all beaches in Puerto Rico are public spaces! This hotel is a must stay if you want cool elegance, outstanding professional service, and a beautiful space!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Overall Satisfied My friend and I spent Memorial Day weekend at the Normandie and enjoyed our stay very much. The staff was warm, friendly and accommodating. We took the public bus (only 25c) into old San Juan and to Isle Verde during the day. At night we would take cabs, but found we were very centrally located to pretty much everything. The beach at the Normandie was less than par so we used the beach next door at the Caribe. There is a Subway sandwhich shop, a Morton steakhouse and a convenience market all within walking distance. They just opened a lounge on the second floor that was popular at night but mostly we went elsewhere for nightlife. The spa was clean and affordable. The pool area was small, but clean and quite. Our room had a stereo system, satellite TV, a mini fridge and the bed was better than most hotel beds you get these days. Overall a pleasant experience and would stay there again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfectly adequate I saw some terrible reviews of this hotel after booking the trip and was terrified of what I would find. Turns out the hotel was beautiful, if a little boring. The hotel has only one restaurant that seems very nice, but is fairly expensive. The atrium is gorgeous, but is usually empty. The rooms were very comfy and nicely decorated. The only thing really lacking at this hotel is a nice pool. The pool is fairly small and not very interesting. It looked like there was a poolside bar, but I don't think it was open for business. Honestly, we spent most of our time at the pool at the Hilton Caribe next door, as was recommended in other reviews. This, by the way, is not something the Hilton welcomes, and they've started checking room keys at the pool. Do not book here if you want a beachfront hotel. There is NO beach here. Otherwise, the location was pretty convenient. It's close to Old San Juan, and also close to the Condado beach area. There's a Subway right across the street, but otherwise no restaurants within walking distance except for a (wonderful) little hole-in-the-wall local cafe with home-cooked breakfast, lunch and dinner for almost nothing frequented mostly by construction workers and landscapers from the Hilton. My kind of place, but not for most tourists, I'm sure.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Normandie Was Charming! We had already booked at the Normandie back in December for spring break 2005 - then saw some negative reviews so was nervous. It was unfounded. It was like stepping back into another era. The staff was very efficient and courteous - the only trouble we had was with renting a vehicle big enough to carry our brood (14 in all!) - but it was handled. They did their best to accomodate our big crowd. We ate breakfast there twice - was very nicely presented, although portions were on the small side. The pool was nicely kept with towels on hand. Their beach wasn't desirable at all, but the public beach within walking distance was gorgeous (not the one by the Caribe - other direction!) - spent one day there just vegging. It is quiet there - the renovations are 99% complete, so you need to go elsewhere for the nightlife. I thought the room was more than adequate - we had a junior suite for three people - we didn't trip over each other - and I've stayed in some places that were no bigger than a broom closet! Old San Juan is easily accessible and it's close to the airport. The only thing I would change about it's location is that there be more restaurant choices within walking distance. We ate a lot of Subway that week! Amazing view of the ocean, especially in the a.m. I'd stay there again, although next time I travel to PR, I intend to spend more time on the Caribbean side of the island. A most enjoyable trip overall!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Hotel, Great Deal - Ignore the negative postings! Apparently, the Normandie has now completed its construction, which can obviously be disruptive and may be the source of negative reviews below, but whatever the case, my wife and I LOVED this hotel! It is a cool art deco gem and the lounge area is really inviting and stylish. Our room was immaculate and positively massive with a view of the water, the bed was one of the most comfortable I've ever slept in and the service was quite good. We had a flat screen tv and cd player in our room and only the bathroom was (very mildly) disappointing, but only by comparison with the comfy, super-stylish look of everything else. If this hotel were in South Miami Beach, it would be $150 a night more expensive. The Normandie isn't a resort hotel with a huge pool and beach, so don't expect that, but you do nevertheless have an adequate pool and beach and those of the Caribe Hilton next door can be very easily borrowed. There is a bus stop 100 yards away that you can take into/out of Old San Juan (25 cents!) The Normandie is a hotel with lots of character and it is clearly on its way back up. Very highly recommended.  
<Date>Mar 22, 2005

<Content>good experience I recently stayed at the normandie, one night before leaving for a cruise. the lobby and main floor is renovated and reminds me of a art deco look. i was very surprised by this - after reading the other reviews. we had the cheapest room in the place (only paid $120/night). <Author>GranReserva
<Content>Good value and location! I spent four nights at the Normandie from 21st Jan 2005. I was a bit worried after having read mostly negative feedback. I come from aself-service society, so I don't expect 24h room service or bar service at the pool. Also you must understand that Normandie is a city hotel - not a resort.   The overall hotel prices in Puerto Rico are too high compared with the most popular holiday destinations in Europe and Asia. Even now, when the Euro trades at 1.28 against the Dollar, only shopping is very cheap in Puerto Rico if you get paid in Euros or Sterlings.Puerto Rico is not an exotic country with perfect beaches or wildlife (execpt Culebra and Vieques islands). The roads are packed with 1.9 million cars. I think that most people visit there because US citizens don't need to have Visas or to exchange foreign money. Sure PR is worth visiting but I expected to see at least as good beaches as in the Mediterranean islands, for example Menorca and Mallorca. Sure, you can't enjoy beaches in Europe in winter. San Juan and Ponce are the only built-up areas that have something to see. The best beach in the mainland was in a private, huge area called Palmas del Mar in the East Coast. Thanks to the local law, the beach is accessible for non-residents after a security check in the gate. It takes 60-90 minutes by car from the Normandie to Palmas del Mar.   I found that the High Season period outside San Juan is only a good idea from the industry to get more profit.   San Juan hotels seemed to be quite fully booked, but elsewhere it was very quiet ( I spent total 17 nights in four hotels). Even Lonely Planet recommends to book hotels well in advance. Only weekends are more busy when the Puerto Ricans head to beaches. You should negotiate the room rate from Sunday to Thursday in the countryside.  The room was spacious, bed comfort very good (not Sheraton),bathroom renovated, TV set and picture OK. However, window was small and located quite far from the bed which made the room dark. Only the 6th floor rooms had balconies. The other negative thing was that there was a thin wooden door between my and and the next room ( I was in the 5th floor). After 18 hours of travelling from home to hotel it was not fun to listen the noise behind that door. However, similar strange door was also found in the four-star el Conquistador resort hotel near Fajardo - with the same problem. During the daytime renovation in the 4th floor could sound nasty, but I did not need the room at that time of a day.   The hotel itself is very beautiful, especially interior. I felt good I did not choose more expensive hotels in Condado or Isla Verde - most of them represent the 1970's concrete style. To be fair, most of these 1970's hotels and other buildings were in good shape - even though not attractive. Isla Verde was nicer area than Condado, but too far away from the main destination- Old SJ. I have seen hundreds of nice historical towns in Europe, Old SJ beats many of them. If I had the money, I would have chosen hotel el Convento inside the Old SJ.   The location was very good. The beach in front of the hotel looked dirty, but just 300m from the hotel to Old SJ direction is a public beach, Balneario Escambron, which was perhaps the best for swimming in San Juan. (According to Lonely Planet, that beach is not recommendable - but I disagree.) Old San Juan, which is almost the only beautiful city area for evening walks in the whole island, is within 30 min walk from the hotel. Also Condado area is within walking distance (taxis are expensive).   I would like to mention the pool area, it was elegant, water was clear and clean - the size and depth of the pool was excellent for a city hotel.   I have no comments on restaurant services, the bar downstairs looked good but there was so cold inside (air condition) I preferred to stay outdoors. Service in the reception was very kind and professional, the hotel has doormen as well - quite nice for a 3-star hotel. I would have given 5/5 without the noise from the neighboring room. It should be eliminated by removing the door between the rooms and filling it with concrete. But as I said the value for money in Puerto Rico hotels is rather poor in their so-called high season. I would have stayed in a 5-star hotel in Madrid, Spain at a lower rate. Hotels, especially outside San Juan should drop their rates at least 40%. For example the Rincon Beach hotel in a remote area costs over 200$ - the parking area was almost empty every time I passed the hotel during 5 days in Rincon.   S.T. Helsinki, Finland   
<Date>Feb 9, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Average hotel for the price We stayed here thru Priceline. After reading the reviews, I was a bit worried but my fears were unfounded. There is still renovation work being done - restaurant is still closed - but it should all be done by end of February. The rooms are very large and clean. We found the staff to be extremely helpful and friendly at all times. The beach is non-existant, but the pool is nice. The Fitness Center is a joke. Don't expect to get a good workout here.The best thing about the hotel is the location. It is close to Old San Juan and has a bus stop right in front. The Caribe Hilton is next door, and has all the amenities you could hope for, including several pools, outdoor bars / cafes, restaurants, shops, even a Starbucks. No one checks to see if you are a guest, so you can pay a small price at the Normandie and enjoy all of the facilities at the Hilton. It's great!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Normandie Hotel - May want to reconsider staying there We stayed at the Hotel Normandie on January 8th. When we booked it the hotel was rated a 3 star hotel. While it is apparent that they are making updates  improvements to the hotel, it is not currently in a condition to be considered 3 star. You can tell that they are working to improve the hotel but it does have a long way to go. They have made improvements to the guest rooms  they were pretty nice. The furniture had all been replaced  our room had a flat screen TV. The bed was comfortable  the room was large. The bathroom was also large  had some recent updates. Be advised that they do NOT provide hair dryers in the bathroom. Some of the areas that need improvement: Rugs in the hallway are soiled  stained The closet in our room had a very musty odor.The elevators are extremely small  very old. They were quite dirty as well.The hotel only has one store, if you can consider it a store. It was more like a closet that was converted to a small convenience store. The hotel had a restaurant but a very limited menu. We did not eat there so can't say if the food was good. When we checked in, we were asked to sign a waiver that the hotel was not responsible for the loss of personal valuables. However when we went to our room, we found that the windows didn't even have locks on them. This was also supposed to be a beach front hotel, but when we went out to the 'beach', we found that it was about a 20 foot stretch of beach that was about 3 feet wide. Definitely not what we were expecting. Don't be fooled about the current condition of the hotel by their website. They make it seem like a great, wonderful hotel but in it's current condition, it certainly is not great  wonderful. It has potential, but it's not there yet.

<Content>Hey, The Normandie Is Okay Don't be misled by all of the nasty reviews.... We sure didn't see it. We arrived on December 20th and stayed for 5 nignts. <Content>Avoid this hotel! Our December experience at the Park Plaza Normandie was as simple as: (1) We had a three room 'suite.' One room had nothing in it at all, and one room only had a desk and no other furniture. The remaining room had the bed, TV unit and clothes rack. (2) Painting was constant and so the paint smells were everpresent. (3) For a suite, we had one very tiny trashcan in the bathroom. (4) On check-in we had to sign a statement that acknowedged that the hotel was not responsible for theft/loss of valuable/personal property. We could not use the room safe since we had an old safe, and they could only find the key for the new room safe, which has yet to be installed. So, as an alternative they offered to hold our valuables in a safe at the desk. When we went to do that we were surprised to watch them take our valuables, put them in a brown paper envelope and leave them in a drawer at the counter labeled: guest packages. (5) The elevators worked sometimes, sometimes they did not. (6) The electricity would cut off for a while every night, and a very LOUD generator would cut on right outside of our room, waking us up. We got used to the room clock flashing all of the time and finally stopped resetting the time. For the price we paid, there was no value in this hotel at all! I would have rather saved the money and slept in the car, rather than have paid them what they charged for a room and get this sort of unpleasant experience. We won't be back.

<Author>Voudre
<Content>Blah...plus terrible service The only thing this big hotel has going for it is its unusual, whimsicalarchitecture - shaped like a grand ship of 'yore, The Normandie. Once inside I felt I had entered the halls of a local public hospital. It had a lackluster cement/tile interior with poor lighting, uneven flooring  all I can remember was the grayness of it all. Running along the circumfrence of the ground flr was a photo exhibit of the original owner of this hotel and his indulgent, ex-showgirl French wife-they were jet setters. These were photos from the 30-40's in tribute to them. Being Puerto Rican, knowing about Puerto Rican culture, values and society, I cringed at this little exhibit. As for my room, it was clean but also as spare as can be, dark and musty. No carpet. All sounds from the hall echoed in. The staff : the worst I've ever experienced in a Puerto Rico hotel. Front desk : RUDE. Impersonal . Totally preoccupied with socializing with each other rather than servicing the customers. What are THESE people doing working in the service industry?? I had a tepid warm breakfast buffet the next morning  checked out after one night. I absolutely, unequivocally, do NOT recommend you stay here. If you cant' find a room in any of the other big hotels in the San Juan/ Condado area, stay at any of the numerous smaller hotels, inns  guesthouses - there are many charming,friendly, small lodgings in the area - check out the WEPA! Website for listings  check reviews. The ones on this site are reliable.

<Author>NYgirl7
<Content>it was okay.... This hotel was decent. the rooms were large and spacious. Don't go there if you want a lot of extras The pool was nice (my husband and I were the only ones using it!). But DO NOT plan to use their beachfront. It's a tiny, dirty patch of sand. This hotel is set apart a little bit from restaurants and other hotels. you should probably rent a car or be prepared to pay lots of cab fares. the bus takes you into old san juan for just 25 cents. but don't take it anywhere else. i made the mistake of trying to take it to the mall. An hour in a crowded bus was NOT FUN. the staff was friendly and helpful at this hotel. so if you are low-maintenance, it's a good deal. if you are looking for luxury and amenities, stay somewhere else!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>not too bad not too good. i was very hesistant to book the normandie bc of all the mixed reviews but went ahead with it anyway. the normandie is a nice hotel. plain, simple and considerably clean. the staff was pleasant, the concierge was very helpful and all in all it was a good stay. the downside is that the beach and pool area are definitely not the greatest. a little deceiving to be honest...the pool overlooks a PUBLIC beach which is filthy and crowded. the hilton next door has the private beach, (what you see from your room). location wise, the hotel is situated 1.5 miles from old san juan, bit of a walk but its do-able and pretty. isla verde, which is where we went to the beach, is a $16 cab ride and about 8 minutes from the hotel. if you're just looking for a clean, pleasant place to sleep..then the Normandie is great. if you're looking for a resort type hotel, try again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Park Plaza Normandie was a good hotel. The Park Plaza Normandie was a step above average. The Jr. Suite was spacious, with a beach view. A couple of lamps needed to have bulbs replaced but never got them. The Continental Breakfast was more than adequate, with fresh fruits, juice, yogurt, different rolls and breads, coffee. However, the other meals were somewhat pricey. The Concierge was very helpful in booking tours. Since it was off-season, the tours were not running every day, and as a result, we did not get a chance to go to Ponce and a coffee plantation. It would be nice to know this kind of information in advance. The hotel had a nice location - right next to Millenium Park, and maybe about 1and 1/2 blocks from Luis Munoz Rivera Park. It's only about a 10 min. taxi ride to Old San Juan.

<Author>infoseek123
<Content>Fair Value, Location ??? The hotel is decent, the rooms are fair, don't expect much. It is located right next to the Hilton, and you can walk to the Hilton in no tiime.There are no restuarants besides the ones at these two hotels which are all a bit pricey. You have to walk about a mile or so to get to a non-hotel restaurants. If you want to Jog, there is a small track behind the hotel to your left. The hotel gym is there for name sake and it just as big as probably your bathroom.You can take the bus from a few blocks away, very cheap 25 cents, yes, in June 2004, it was 25 cents/person to Old San Juan/anywhere the bus goes. It takes about 15 minutes. It might be a good place to stay for two or so nights, I couldn't stay here for more than that. Condodo is another alternative, much more choices as far as food is concerned and you can walk to that area from here, it is 15 minutes away, about 1 mile.Opposite side from Condodo, If you walk towards the stadium, go behind the stadium through the parking lot, and make a right when you get to the main street and walk another 1/2 mile, there is a KFC there and a few local restuarants. You feel safe and this is a U.S. territory. Please email me if you have detailed questions.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Normandie has great location My boyfriend and I wanted to go on a getaway when we say an ad on TV for Puerto Rico. So we checked it out on aavacations.com and booked it for March, 2002. It was about ten minutes from the airport and upon arriving a bellboy took our luggage as we signed in. Then Jose, the bellboy took us to our room while telling us the history of the hotel and then told us briefly about the town and some sites we should see. The beach isn't huge and it's not pure white sand like the rest of the carribean, but there were never more than 4 people on it and it's secluded, there's a more public beach a block or so away also. We ate at the hotel, but also there's a deli across the road and other restaurants a block or so away. Also the Normandie is in walking distance of the Old San Juan and the newer casino/hotel area. But our favorite part about the Normandie was the service, neither of us spoke any spanish, so they booked all of our tours for us, and when we had a problem with one of our tours, it was the hotel who above and beyond to care of it for us. This hotel was perfect for us and we are planning on going back in Aug of 04.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not a resort, but good value otherwise If you need a place to stay for a night before or after your cruise, this is a fine value. If you are looking for a resort destination, stay at the Caribe Hilton next door for twice the price. I found the Normandie to be a pleasant older hotel. The room was large. The decor was nothing special. The staff was helpful. It's about 2 miles to Old San Juan. The beach, pool, etc. are not the strong points of this hotel. Room service was adequate; the food was nothing special but nicely presented and tasty enough.

Make sure that you use gorilla proof luggage when visiting SJ. The luggage handling at the airport is rough.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Normandie did not delivered on (website) promise On the good side, the hotel is nicely done, and reasonably well decorated, but lacking in a decent community area to hang out in, other than a small internal bar. Given all the good views available, they should have put the bar one floor up with a front (street) or rear (beach) terrace access. Food was very good and the breakfast, lunch and dinner buffets were excellent values. The room (713) was big, roomy, with big windows. The room service was competent, quick and clean.On the bad side, the hotel's air conditioning system is noisy, unreliable (there seems to be only 2 settings: freezing, or not working.........at least in room 713). My travel mate and I requested room with 2 beds (2 REAL beds, anyway), and only got 1 king, and a convertible sofa. No other rooms were available. Also, the website shows a photo of 2 tennis courts alongside the hotel, and they list tennis as one of the available activities, a BIG reason why we chose to stay there.......but they don't tell you the courts belong to the Caribe Hilton next door, who wouldn't let us use them. Lastly, the scuba diving headquarters are NOT. They have no real access to good diving, and have limited equipment and personnel. Try some of the island's real specialists for scuba (like in Fajardo or Rincon)Their private beach is a tiny 50' x 10' strip of wet sand, cut off from the open sea, and only accessible off the hotel grounds through a locked gate with a security buzzer!!The pool area was OK, with an abandoned and unused bar, lacking any poolside service, a pity if you want to really service your guests.While the people at the Normandie, and in the various bars and restaurants in the area are friendly and welcoming, I can think of plenty of other places in the Caribean I'd rather go to. It may be a better place for families that want a controlled area, by the water, and close to town.Personally, I won't be back at the Normandie anytime soon.  
<Date>Jan 14, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The stay at this was Horrible, I will never stay here again!!! It started with a noisy air conditioning system and an inordinate and loud banging of what sounded like heavy furniture being moved around at the early part of the morning. I politely requested a transfer from the first room (rm. 511). I was placed in a room that the bathroom had a leak --- the ice bucket had garbage in it. The door to the terrace was not furnished with a curtain to block early morning sunrays. Once again I was transferred to another room (209) this room was more a kin to a maids room, small and had access to the terrace open from a public area of the hotel. Lastly, I was transferred again to another room that I finally accepted with resolve --- after all this was, my last night and I would never stay in this hotel ever again. To the credit of the staff, I can say that to say the least they acted somewhat embarrassed at having to keep finding resolution to the problems that kept arising throughout my stay. I would blame top management... the rooms were lacking in proper cleaning, the air-conditioning system in the rooms that i stayed in need servicing. I found myself appologizing to my Lady friend every night for the Normandie surprise.Room service should not be so restrictive, in that this service should be open later --- reason being that the hotel itself is a distance from off premise eateries. I want to state at this time that I have stayed all over the carribean and it is a sad stae of affairs that a place that needs tourist dollars is so shably kept. The resorts in the Dominican Republic --- that I have stayed in operate better than your hotel--- and remember that it is in a third world country that their currency is a peso. I am a member of a few groups holding different positions in each. If I am asked if I can recommend a good place to stay while visiting the Island of Puerto Rico --- I assuredly would not utter the name of the Normandie in San Juan.
